海外星訊 269

— 邨

據美國百老匯一家電影雜誌裏載着··一九三一年全年中，好萊塢有三十七個明星結婚，去年前九個月内，有三十四個和他的妻子或她的丈夫到法庭上去離婚，打算另訂新歡。結結離離，在他們腦海裏，算得怎麽一回事！

曼蓮黛德麗許在攝完「金髮女神」後，就不見了。雖然消息最鐅通的訪員，也找不出她的踪跡來。有的造謠說她被丈夫休棄了，有的甚至說她到德國去了。可是現在消息傅來，曼蓮因爲拍SongofSongs一片，沒有司登堡（Ｖonsterberg）做她的導演，就隱藏起來了。

笑匠卓别林，早有拍攝拿破崙影片之意，可是時間在不斷的過去，他對於這片的描墓，似乎更在嚴密考慮了。事實上，他現在告訴幾個很知己的朋友說，他不再做喜劇了。因此，有許多人相信他要開攝有聲片了。

小明星黎鏗 270

— 蔣青

在我國一般影星中，最缺乏的人材是童角。鄭小秋現在已經成了明星公司小生的台柱，但二春的黃金時代丨武俠片最盛時丨也過去了。這中國賈克科根一流的人物，却還沒有產生。

聯華公司去年攝「人道」一片中，我們發現了一個燦爛的天才丨黎鏗，極受觀衆贊美。他今年才五歲，說着一口粤話，天眞爛漫，可愛異常。他是聯華第一塲主任黎民偉的愛子。自從「人道」映出後，他最近又將拍「幼年中國，」由他主演。他的國語發音也很準確，南京路永生公司曾請他播间唱歌呢。

他山之石

戰地歷險記中的高跟皮鞋及軍用地圖 271

— 霄玉虹

我深知道中國電影界苦楚有許多地方，都是心有餘而力不足的，所以批評電影的人也都應加以諒解而不可深責的。不過在可能範圍内的小動作上，也極應加以注意，整如戰地歷險記中，似乎有這麽兩點是不合乎情理的；

丁明霞因冒險戰地，所以才換了一身鄕下人的裝束，不過當他被囚而自願出首時，脫去其長統老布禨，忽然現出一雙高跟的皮鞋來，這似乎是令人莫名其妙！若以高跟鞋套上長統老布襪，再穿上男人鞋，這是不可能的事，若說從匪營臨時找到的，那也是不合情理的，

丁明霞的盜軍用地圖，在全劇中是一個很大的關鍵，但是我們要曉得他所盜的一張軍用地圖是一張什麽地圖？我可發誓說；他所盜的，是一張極普通的中國全圖，這也是不合情理的，因在一張極普通的中國全圖上，計劃某一個地方的軍事行動，亦屬滑天下之大稽了，何况丁明霞千辛萬苦的盜回來，官長們交相稱譽而引爲奇功呢？

以上兩點並非吹毛求疪實事所不能的事，不知導演先以爲何如？

梨渦和酒渦 272

— 澄

靠近女子芳唇的兩類上的美渦，呌梨渦。也呌酒渦。定名雖不同，用意實如出一轍。梨是甜的，多水。酒是瓊漿，統而言之，皆是令人可愛嘉吃的。十六日本刋上，我見到元君的投稿，覺得胡姗的出言吐語，大有和姊姊胡蝶爭梨渦的味兒。其實賢姊姊不要爭，因爲那美窟　兒，有兩種說法的，我們以後簡直呌··梨渦蝶，酒渦姗，好了。這様一來，不但各標異斾，能使人特别注視，並且大有並架齊驅芳名千古之槪！不知其他明星，如梁氏三花，還有什麽共同的特微沒有？要請觀影的諸君多多注視一下才好！

「火柴大王」本事（十四） 273

— 希孟譯

安東尼亞斯加接底

巴黎德洛希路三百十九號

有一天一條漁船拖進了波爾的海上一個小島的港口，船上跑下來一個人，是一個身材矮小的意大利人，面貌很透狡獪的神氣。那條漁船卸下了客人，就開走了。那人等船開走了，就拾了小徑向一所避暑的空屋子走。走到了，敲門。開門就是保羅克魯爾。他開了門，將那人往裏一拉，門又緊地關上了。

「你是不是要向我購買一些重要的文件？」那意利人問。

「先讓我看看，」保羅說。「這裏沒有别人。」保羅看見那意大利人從身邊抽了一個橡皮布的皮包。

「這裏有五十張意大利政府的國庫券，」他慢慢地打開那皮包，一每張的數目係一百萬元」，他將牠放在保羅的手裏。

「先生，這個同眞的一般無二，或比眞的還要好些。」他狡滑的目光緊緊地釘住了保羅的眼睛。「先生你要多少張？」

「五十張一齊要，」保羅斷然地說。

那意大利人驟然聽見，驚喜出乎意外。他想敲竹槓的機會來了。况且人家買了這一大筆假庫券，把柄就在他手裏，此後隨時可以寻到他，眞是一生吃着不盡的好主顧了。

保羅看了那意利人，很奇怪微微一笑。

「斯加拉底，我現在先付你五千元，表示我眞心同你交易的誠意，其餘的，欵項，明天在巴黎付清。你看好不好」？

「很好很好，先生，」好意大利人回說。

保羅拿出他的皮夾子，抽出互張一千元的票子，那意大利人接收了反覆的騐視了一下，點點頭收了起來。

「我順便帶你上陸吧，」保羅向他說。「你要進瑞典境内並不難吧？」他故意的閒問着。　　斯加拉底笑了。

「我自己發自己的護照，自己簽己的字，我進了瑞典境，誰都不知道。」

保羅的眼中，放出奇異的光彩。他是再滿意不過了。他所要知道的。就是沒有人知道他在瑞典境内。

他們二人一同踏進了快艇。斯加拉底手裏有了錢，很快活的坦然坐在船的後梢，那船風馳電掣一般地在波浪中穿進去。忽然地保羅寛魯爾將輪盤一轉丨斯加拉底哎呀一聲，滾下水中，浪花四濺，人已不知去向了。克魯爾頭也沒有回過來看一看，一直地風馳電掣地去了。他一個人很安詳地上了岸。

Page 23

1933.01.20

Today's Headline Highlights 1

Domestic: Japanese Planes Bomb Kairu County Town; British Envoy Lampson Arrives in Xiamen; Various Circles in Nanchang Send Another Telegram Urging Chiang to Enter Jiangxi to Suppress Bandits

Foreign: League of Nations Maintains Five-Power Resolution Draft, Eliminates Invitation to US and Russia; Hoover and Roosevelt to Meet Today to Discuss Far East Issues; Millions of Tons of Australian Wheat Flour Shipped to China

Shanghai: Ma Zhanshan's Representative Hosts Press Conference to Report Progress; Muslims Receive Telegram from Xinjiang Refuting Rumors of Muslim Uprising; Pirates Raid Dahua Steamer off Wusong Port

League of Nations Courting Japan, Sacrificing Principles

Hoping for a Resuscitation Through Mediation 2

Canceling the Invitation to the US and Russia to Uphold Last Year's Five-Power Draft Agreement

Great Disappointment that Our Country's Requests for Amendments Were Ignored

(Nanjing) Our delegation in Geneva telegraphed to the capital on the 19th, reporting on the situation of the Committee of Nineteen's meeting on the 18th. The Japanese side strongly opposed inviting the US and Russia to participate and explicitly denying the puppet organization. During the 18th meeting, it was indicated that the invitation to the US and Russia could be withdrawn, but it was hoped that Japan would fully accept the remaining articles. It was decided to give Japan a final opportunity for consideration, with a continued meeting scheduled for the 20th. If the Japanese side does not agree, the failure of mediation will be reported to the General Assembly. (19th, Central News Agency dispatch)

(Geneva) Many believe that the proposal to withdraw the invitation to the US and Russia will not necessarily salvage the situation, as mediation has already essentially failed. However, it is now a gesture, giving Japan various opportunities to avoid a break. The Chinese side views yesterday's proceedings as disappointing. It neither fulfills China's demands nor strengthens the resolution. There is no word of criticism for Japan's actions, and no clear rejection of recognition of [Manchukuo]. Although this is the final resolution, it does not indicate that new proposals from Japan will not be accommodated. Independent observers view yesterday's meeting with indifference, believing its outcome is a major concession to Japan. The suggestion not to invite non-member states to participate in mediation is already a Japanese victory, so there is no need to be overly pessimistic about the situation because the door to negotiations is still open. The above are the views of various parties related to the League of Nations regarding the current state of affairs. The confusion of the situation is evident. (19th, Reuters dispatch)

(Geneva) After a three-hour meeting of the Committee of Nineteen today, it can be considered virtually certain that the US and Russia will no longer be invited to participate in resolving the Manchurian issue. It is reported that the names of the US, Russia, and other countries were not mentioned at all during today's meeting and were consistently referred to as non-member states, which is also noteworthy. It is also heard that the proposal to remove the invitation to the US and Russia was originally put forward by Chairman Hymans and Secretary-General Drummond, with the support of several other countries. As for the position of British Foreign Secretary Simon on this matter, the spokesperson for the British delegation stated that he was not yet prepared to comment. However, some diplomats here claim that even if the US and Russia were invited, it would be highly questionable whether the two countries would accept. Therefore, if inviting them would place Japan in a position of being responsible for disrupting mediation, it would be better to decide not to invite them.

Japanese representative Matsuoka stated that if this renewed effort to resolve the Manchurian issue fails again, the committee seems likely to consider adopting Article 15, Paragraph 4 of the Covenant. However, he has just received instructions that, regarding proceeding with Article 15, Paragraph 3, if there is a motion to invoke Paragraph 4, he must seek further instructions from the government.

It is currently believed that regardless of the direction the League of Nations takes, Japan will wait until the League of Nations General Assembly issues its report and recommendations before deciding whether to withdraw from the League. However, even if Japan decides to withdraw, it will only take effect two years after issuing a notice, at which time it will have fulfilled all its obligations under the Covenant. The League of Nations, even after receiving the Japanese notice, will still be able to hear the Sino-Japanese dispute as before.

Although some here support the view that the draft resolution prepared by the Committee of Nineteen last December cannot be further discussed, the British claim that the instructions given to Chairman Hymans by the committee at that time had sufficient flexibility to allow him to reconsider it. (18th, Guomin News)

(Geneva) Today's meeting of the Committee of Nineteen is being given great importance by all sectors. Furthermore, the situation at the League of Nations has now reached an extremely tense state, as the amendments proposed by the League, secretly manipulated by Japan, are opposed not only by China but also by many other member states.

The League of Nations community in Geneva views the note delivered by Japanese representative Matsuoka with great indifference and is particularly concerned about Japan's resolute rejection of the US and Russia's participation in mediation. What is now being discussed is whether British Foreign Secretary Simon will advocate convening a special meeting of the League of Nations General Assembly to pass the Lytton Report. According to observers, Britain's actions are merely to express dissatisfaction with Japan's actions but may not be able to follow the views of the powers and make the League of Nations clearly point out that it does not recognize the existence of [Manchukuo]. Recently, the Paris Morning Post carried a Tianjin dispatch stating that Japanese General Nakamura issued a declaration stating that, for security reasons, Japan may need to occupy Beiping and the key points along the Ping-Sui Railway to prevent China's continued mobilization. The record of this here has drawn much criticism. (18th, Guomin News)

(Geneva) A certain important Japanese spokesperson stated today, "We are here to seek compromise, not confrontation. If the Special Committee of Nineteen destroys the possibility of direct Sino-Japanese compromise and turns this into a dispute between the League of Nations and Japan, it would be truly inconceivable. We are not without hope of salvaging this unfortunate event." The Chinese side is now adopting an attitude of cautious hope. Guo Taiqi told a Reuters reporter that there is now reason to believe that the facts are gradually moving towards the right track and that the Japanese will be forced to restrain themselves. Guo also stated that, in any case, there is still much to rely on the Special Committee of Nineteen to handle the issue of preparing a report on the Lytton Report, and that the moral and legal judgment that China has long hoped for from the League of Nations seems not far off. (19th, Reuters dispatch)

(Tokyo) The situation of the Committee of Nineteen has reverted to its state on December 20th of last year. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs is conducting negotiations with the League of Nations with the following guidelines: 1. Japan is quite satisfied that the League of Nations acknowledges the withdrawal of the invitation to the US and Russia as a matter of course. 2. However, this cannot be used as an exchange condition to require Japan to accept the old resolution of December 20th of last year. 3. The League of Nations should organize a committee of the four countries with the closest relationship to the Sino-Japanese issue—Britain, France, Italy, and Belgium—with the aim of assisting direct Sino-Japanese negotiations. 4. To clarify its nature and powers, this committee should remove the term "mediation" and cannot unconditionally adopt the Lytton Report as the basis for its deliberations. 5. The rationale for the resolution should be changed to the form of a statement by the chairman, and the words denying [Manchukuo] should be deleted, and other necessary parts of the resolution should be amended. (19th, Dentsu dispatch)

(Geneva) Yesterday, the Committee of Nineteen asked the Japanese delegation whether Japan would accept the draft resolution passed last December if the section on "inviting non-League of Nations member states to participate in the mediation committee" were deleted. Regarding this question, the Japanese delegation has already requested instructions from the Tokyo government. According to Japanese sources, the situation here remains chaotic until Japan's reply arrives. However, the most responsible figures in the Japanese delegation believe that it would be beyond their expectations if the country's reply satisfies the Committee of Nineteen. They are seriously considering that the Committee of Nineteen may need to abandon the mediation procedure and adopt Article 15, Paragraph 4 of the League of Nations Covenant. Japanese sources anticipate that the Committee of Nineteen, even if not unanimously, will at least obtain a majority in favor of this measure. It is not yet known what attitude the Japanese delegation will take if this situation occurs. External news about this matter is somewhat premature. The most responsible Japanese figures firmly state that even if the Committee of Nineteen insists on adopting the procedure of Article 15, Paragraph 4, and submits a report to the General Assembly with recommendations without the consent of the parties involved, Japan will not immediately withdraw from the League of Nations. The Japanese delegation will at least remain in Geneva for several days to observe the progress as an observer, to know the content of the report, and then leave Geneva, at least temporarily not cooperating with the League of Nations. In that case, Japan will not break with the League of Nations and leave abruptly. The attitude it takes will be roughly the same as that taken by Argentina towards the League of Nations several years ago. (19th, Havas dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Imperial Government believes that the Committee of Nineteen's decision on the 18th to use the draft resolution of December 15th as the basis for future negotiations is not satisfied merely by withdrawing the invitation to non-member states. Regarding the composition and powers of the small committee and the adoption of Chapters 9 and 10 of the Lytton Report in their entirety, it seems that important amendments will be proposed. Considering the spirit of the Drummond Plan, it seems that a solution can still be found between the League of Nations and the Japanese Imperial Government's requested amendments. However, the most difficult point is to change the rationale to a chairman's statement and to withdraw the expression of non-recognition of [Manchukuo] in the final item. However, the smaller countries seem to consistently adhere to the original plan. Therefore, in the worst-case scenario, a maximum amount of concessions seems to be considering the following compromise proposals: 1. The rationale is to be a chairman's statement to reduce its effect. 2. The Japanese delegation should make a statement of opposition to the chairman's statement, declaring the rationality and political significance of recognizing [Manchukuo], etc. This statement should be recorded in the minutes. (19th, Den-tsu dispatch)

Special Committee

Yesterday's Meeting Situation 3

(Geneva) The Special Committee of Nineteen met at 4 PM on the 18th. After discussing for three hours, it decided to propose to Japan:

Cancel the Invitation to the US and Russia to Participate 4

If the clause inviting the US and Russia to join the mediation is canceled, then Japan should accept the draft resolution of December 20th and the other clauses of the explanatory memorandum. Thus, Japan now faces the choice of whether to accept the Lytton Report as the basis for mediation or to bear the responsibility of breaking with the League of Nations in principle, but not in matters of law (such as inviting non-member states to participate).

Mediation is Expected to Ultimately Fail 5

The League of Nations, observing today's developments, expects the Special Committee of Nineteen to report the failure of mediation to the League of Nations General Assembly within a few days. If Japan cannot agree to withdraw its remaining objections, this move is unavoidable. Observing today's meeting situation, the Special Committee of Nineteen carefully considered everything when making this decision. The main point of today's discussion was not to sacrifice substance when arguing over events that everyone recognizes as empty shadows, as it is still undecided whether the US and Russia are willing to participate in mediation. Furthermore, the news from Washington in the past few days has indicated the indefinite continuation of Stimson's Far East policy. There were more listeners at today's meeting of the Special Committee than before, and journalists expressed great patience with the delay of the meeting.

Soft and Hard Factions Engaged in Close Combat 6

And recognized this as a war of short swords between those who advocate mediation and those who advocate strong measures. The Special Committee discussed Japan's proposals for quite a long time and ultimately felt that there were several points that could not be accepted. At the same time, it also studied China's amendments, feeling that Japan's amendments were sufficient to weaken the Special Committee's resolution, while China's amendments made this resolution even stronger. However, the Special Committee felt that it was more appropriate to deal with Japan's points of opposition first and then consider China's proposals. Chairman Hymans explained Japan's insistence that non-member states must not participate in the dispute and read out various draft resolutions.

Representatives of Small Countries Uphold Justice 7

Irish representative Lester, who is seen as the spokesperson for small countries, asked what degree of necessary relationship the other points raised by Japan have to the resolution of the Sino-Japanese dispute. Swiss representative Motta spoke a great deal, not recognizing that Japan's opposition to the cooperation of non-member states has good reasons in law, but saying that he did not want to hinder this issue with legal arguments, as the key point is to protect the true substantive effectiveness of the resolution. Many speakers expressed the opinion that Japan was not prepared to accept the full text of the draft resolution and the explanatory memorandum. However, it was agreed to ask Chairman Hymans to contact Japanese representative Matsuoka in order to find Japan's reply. Hymans agreed on the spot, and the meeting then ended.

Japan Bears Responsibility for the Failure of Mediation 8

Today's discussions in the Special Committee were sometimes very激昂, but the result was unanimous, and even Irish representative Lester said that the result was very satisfactory. The Special Committee believes that there should not be much difficulty in persuading the Chinese representative to abandon its amendments and agree not to invite the US and Russia to join the mediation. The general opinion is that the Special Committee has adopted a quick compromise, which can make Japan, if it does not accept it, bear the responsibility of breaking, and if it accepts it, then, as a certain special committee member said, it will just expose Japan's boastful deceit.

The League of Nations Exposes Weaknesses Everywhere 9

It is heard that someone proposed that if there are no other changes, the explanatory memorandum can be used as the chairman's statement. The Special Committee did not oppose this proposal, as this move can give both parties the right to make reservations, and at the same time can ease the general situation. However, this cannot be decided until the issue of the resolution is resolved. Everyone expects that the situation will develop rapidly in the next few days. Although the current crisis has been缓, it has not been saved.

Special Committee of Nineteen Issues Communiqué 10

The communiqué was issued at 8:12 PM tonight. The text is as follows: Today, the Special Committee of Nineteen studied the proposals of the Japanese government received by the chairman this morning and felt that its proposals did not conform to the methods approved by this committee and sent to both parties on many fundamental points. One of the main points of opposition of the Japanese government is the participation of representatives of non-member states in resolving disputes submitted to the League of Nations. If this point is Japan's only opposition to the original text of the resolution, then the Special Committee feels that it is not impossible to discuss with both parties to resolve the dispute. Therefore, the Special Committee believes that it is necessary to seek information again, willing to know whether Japan is prepared to accept the draft resolution prepared by the Special Committee last December after this difficulty is resolved. The Special Committee then asked the chairman to contact the Japanese delegation on this point together with the Secretary-General of the League of Nations and then proceed to talk to the Chinese delegation, as the Special Committee believes that it is necessary to first ascertain the reply of the Japanese delegation. The next meeting of the Special Committee is scheduled for Friday. (18th, Reuters dispatch)

Instigated by the Japanese

London Specters Manifest 11

Ding [Shiyuan], a traitor, issues false declarations to conduct counter-propaganda

Our embassy in England strongly denounces his lies

(London) The declaration by [Manchukuo] representative Ding Shiyuan that Rehe Province is subordinate to Manchuria has now been denied by the Chinese side in London, saying that Rehe has always been included in the Chinese territory. When the Manchu emperor entered China, the province was occupied. The Chinese embassy in London declares that [we must never sit idly by and watch the loss of our territory. Rehe is an integral part of Chinese territory, and we must rise up to defend it. The Japanese army's attack on Rehe may be delayed until March due to weather conditions, which will give us a temporary respite. We must know how to handle ourselves, but this 休战 is purely due to weather conditions, so it cannot last long. This is knowable.] (19th, Havas dispatch)

(London) Ding Shiyuan, representative of the puppet Manchukuo, has arrived in London after passing through Moscow, Warsaw, Berlin, Geneva, and Paris and has issued a declaration. Now, according to the principle of recording everything heard, the various points said are summarized below for reference. He said "I am a former Chinese military officer, now coming to Europe to defend [Manchukuo]. Rumors about this [new country] are often inaccurate. We have not been able to formally correct them at any time, because so far, only Japan has recognized the existence of [Manchukuo]. However, we are not in a hurry to seek the formal recognition. We trust in the power of facts, and the facts can defend us. As for what we have already implemented, since 1930, all foreign debts have been guaranteed and repaid. Our first batch of payments can reach 55% of the total amount of foreign debt, of which 30% was repaid in 1931, 25% in 1932, and the remaining 45% will be repaid in 20 years, plus interest at 3%, which is more than what China has ever done. Also, the National Bank has stabilized the currency. The budget for September 1932 to June 1933 has been finalized. Only the customs system remains the same, and the customs officials have been replaced. China has imposed separate taxes on [Manchukuo] goods, so we have no choice but to use the same method to deal with it. The Manchu army initially had 200,000 people and has now been reduced to 100,000. This is unknown to the outside world. The reason is that soldiers are paid by name, so the number still appears to be decreasing. Our soldiers are now fighting alongside the Japanese army, but they are not, as rumored, attacking Rehe, but only seeking to defend Rehe. The province, for centuries, has been an integral part of Manchuria, along with Fengtian, Jilin, and Heilongjiang provinces. Rehe is outside the Great Wall, and has always been the hunting ground for the emperors of the Qing Dynasty. On the Chinese side, the province is not very important, but on the [Manchukuo] side, it is different from the [national] perspective. We will certainly fight for the province with all our strength, but Zhang Xueliang will certainly not fight. The result of this battle will be enough to destroy his army, so there is no need to worry too much about the war. Manchuria will be satisfied once it restores its original borders and will no longer think of crossing the Great Wall except when provoked. However, there must be a neutral zone on the Great Wall. [Manchukuo] is an independent country, not a Japanese colony. [Manchukuo] has a national flag and a national anthem. What it has given to Japan is what Japan has already obtained from China through treaties. Since the declaration of independence on February 18, it has been approved by a free referendum by the people. Manchuria is only restoring its position 300 years ago before the Qing Dynasty ruled mainland China." Ding Shiyuan still has a week's stay in London and will purchase a warship for the training of naval personnel. After that, he will go to Paris, Brussels, Rome, etc., and then return to Changchun. (18th, Havas dispatch)

Japanese Marines Change to Using

Japanese Swords 12

(Tokyo) The Navy, based on the experience of actual combat in the Shanghai Incident, felt that it was inconvenient for the Marine Corps members to only use military swords for command. This time, the correction is that it is convenient to use the old Japanese swords in actual combat, and this article is recorded in the Marine Corps regulations. (19th, Reuters dispatch)

Deterioration of US-Japan Relations

Important Meeting Between Roosevelt and Hoover Today 13

Following the Old Ways of Xiao Gui Cao Sui in Far East Policy

Resumption of Diplomatic Relations with Russia to be Realized Soon

(Washington) President Hoover and President-elect Roosevelt are scheduled to meet on Friday. What they will discuss will be the US-Japan relations involved in the Far East situation. Roosevelt has made it clear in his declaration to the public that he will continue Hoover and Stimson's Far East policy. The repeated statements of the US policy towards China and the repeated violations of the rights of Americans and their industries in the Far East, such as the destruction of the Yokohama Shokai Company and the Osaka American City Bank branch, and the beating of the US consul in Shenyang by the Japanese, have all made the tension between the two countries even greater. It is rumored that people in the Japanese Ministry of the Army are distributing newspaper news that can incite anti-American sentiment, and the Ministry of the Army is paying no attention to it. The United States is even more angered by this news. (19th, Reuters dispatch)

(New York) Today, it was learned from reliable sources that after the new US President Roosevelt takes office, the United States' diplomatic policy on major current issues, except for war debts, will all remain the same as before and will continue to progress. It is said that this decision is the result of Roosevelt's meeting with Stimson, as Stimson's recommendations are completely consistent with Davis's recommendations, with few differences. Therefore, Roosevelt is determined to follow the old ways and not change from the past. According to a certain key member of the Democratic Party, this can be called Roosevelt's policy on issues such as disarmament, the Far East, the world economy, and the relationship between the United States and the League of Nations. However, this policy will certainly progress. Roosevelt's acceptance of Hoover's invitation to meet at the White House today is one proof of this. It is said that the two sides will mainly discuss diplomatic events, and the Far East issue is expected to be considered first. As for Roosevelt's position, it is heard that he will insist on maintaining the 5:5:3 ratio of the British, American, and Japanese navies and must maintain it until a better method is obtained. It is also heard that the new president will advocate building the strongest possible navy within the reasonable and feasible limits of reducing military spending and will never allow the national defense force to be weakened and will advocate adding warships to the treaty limits, but at the same time will seek genuine disarmament. As for the Far East issue, it is said that he agrees with the current policy of not recognizing what is obtained by military aggression. Also, regarding the World Economic Conference, it is heard that Roosevelt's policy is practically the same as Hoover's policy, but he may not be as insistent on limiting the scope of the agenda, and he advocates that in addition to convening an economic conference, existing diplomatic agencies should also begin meetings, hoping to mutually reduce tariffs. It is said that this plan has been supported by Roosevelt's adviser Colonel House, who has thoroughly studied the impact of the Republican Party's high taxes. As for the issue of the United States joining the International Court of Justice, because Peck's advocacy of joining has aroused a reaction of disapproval from the public, it is heard that Roosevelt will at least temporarily shelve it and will handle it when there is a need to deal with it in the future. Also, regarding the issue of recognizing Soviet Russia, it is heard today that Roosevelt has not yet decided, so he has not yet expressed his position and will probably declare his attitude at the time of his inauguration or within a short period of time. As for Roosevelt's war debt plan, no hints have been obtained from key members of the Democratic Party, but it is expected that it will differ from Hoover's position. It is rumored that the Democratic government will favor agreeing on a total amount and issuing international bonds, but when asked about this, key members of the party refused to confirm or deny it. (18th, Guomin News)

Japan's Administration of Various Islands

Installation of Fortress Works 14

The United States is Extremely Concerned

But Denies Encouraging the League of Nations to Investigate

(Washington) With the current attempt in Geneva to resolve the Sino-Japanese dispute apparently reaching a dangerous situation, the Far East situation has become more important than all international issues. It has also been reported here that the League of Nations, in view of Japan's potential withdrawal, is now planning to investigate the Japanese-administered islands in the Pacific, and that the United States has also encouraged the investigation. The State Department immediately denied this, saying that the United States has never encouraged the League of Nations to investigate the current situation of the mandated territories or Japan's installation of fortress works on these islands. Also, European news reports that if Japan withdraws from the League of Nations and still retains the mandated territories, the United States will be extremely concerned because of the danger to the Philippines. People in the State Department also declined to comment on this, only saying that the United States has never made any statements to the League of Nations, nor has it indicated to the League of Nations that Japan has installed fortress works on several islands. Later, the Japanese ambassador's office was asked whether Japan had installed fortress works on the mandated territories, and it was said that Japan had dredged several seaports to dock fishing boats and that there were no fortress works of any kind. Japan has fulfilled all its obligations on the islands. As for the rumor that the United States encouraged the League of Nations to investigate, it is not known how it originated, but it is definitely not from the Japanese side. Since Japan's administration of a part of the islands in the Pacific, there have been rumors from time to time that fortress works will be installed, but after Japan's solemn denial, they have been laid to rest. (18th, Guomin News)

The Enemy is Advancing Towards Lingyuan and Chaoyang Counties

Japanese Planes Bomb Kairu County 15

Enemy Cavalry Assembles in the Dashizizu Area

Feng Zhanhai's Troops Shoot Down a Japanese Plane

(Beiping) The Chief of Staff of Rehe, Li Zanting, reported from Chengde to Beiping that the Japanese troops at Nanling bombarded our positions once on the evening of the 17th at 8 PM. There was no contact on the morning of the 18th until this morning. The 6th, 7th, and 8th Divisions of the Japanese troops stationed in Lingnan are rapidly advancing towards Lingchao counties. The enemy troops of Sanjian Zheng are also advancing from their original station in Beipiao, reaching a location five li from Nanling. The Japanese armored vehicles in Nanling have removed their gun covers and appear ready to fire south towards our positions. On the morning of the 18th, two Japanese planes flew to Chaoyang for reconnaissance but did not drop bombs. At 11 AM, another Japanese plane took off from Wangjia Youfang in Kairu and was shot down by the Righteous Army of Feng Zhanhai using anti-aircraft artillery, destroying the plane and killing the enemy. In Kairu, the Righteous Armies of Feng Zhanhai and Li Haiqing are still engaged in fierce fighting with the Japanese army, which has not stopped. The residents of Kairu are terrified of enemy bombings and are fleeing to Chengde. There have been no major losses recently. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Rehe army reported from its defense area to Beiping that the Japanese army at Chaoyang Temple has been harassing our Nanling positions for days since the 15th. Our army has remained calm throughout. If the enemy advances, we will launch a fierce head-on attack. Because our terrain is steep and we are positioned high, the enemy has launched several fierce attacks but has not succeeded. Now the enemy has changed its strategy and plans to harass Lingnan County from the south. According to reports from the front, the enemy cavalry brigade has advanced to the Dashizizu area on the Rehe border and is concentrating there. Traitors bought by the puppet state are active in Yaowang Temple. The situation in Lingnan is extremely tense. Tang Yulin has transferred a certain unit to provide assistance. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Yesterday afternoon, four Japanese planes suddenly arrived in Kairu, carrying more than a dozen heavy bombs. They bombed the county seat, dropping five bombs on East Main Street in the city, destroying four civilian houses. One was in a certain person's backyard, with no damage. The garrison used anti-aircraft guns to fire, and the enemy planes left. (19th Special Dispatch)

Large-Scale Invasion Possible Before the Spring Festival 17

(Beiping) The Japanese army's plan to invade Rehe is actively underway. Most of the Japanese and puppet troops are concentrated in Jinxi and the Rehe border area. Current Commentary

What Comes First: Repelling Foreign Aggression or Internal Pacification? 26

The greatest problems facing our country today are foreign aggression and internal turmoil. Foreign aggression is urgent, and internal turmoil is also urgent. Therefore, when discussing national salvation today, it inevitably comes down to two paths: internal pacification and repelling foreign aggression.

However, under the current circumstances, when we weigh the priorities, which comes first: repelling foreign aggression or internal pacification? This is a major problem standing in our way. A slight difference can lead to a great error. If this problem cannot be resolved, our work of national salvation will ultimately have no way to advance.

Those who advocate that internal pacification must come before repelling foreign aggression say: Today's war against Japan is a war of the entire nation. It requires the total mobilization of the entire people. In other words, it requires a sound political system and the combined efforts of all the people to exert their full strength and deal with the violent Japanese. However, looking back at the country, there are divergent opinions among parties and factions, strong warlords are dividing and occupying territory, wars and chaos occur from time to time, bandits are everywhere, young people are resentful, and people are panic-stricken. How can such a scattered and disintegrating national force deal with the violent Japanese? Therefore, if we want to repel foreign aggression today, we must first achieve internal pacification.

Our opinion is exactly the opposite.

Why? Because the reason why our country has developed this phenomenon today is precisely because the government has no consistent policy or decisive action towards foreign countries. Precisely because there is no consistent policy, the people are panicked and at a loss. Precisely because there is no decisive action, the people are resentful and dissatisfied. The disaster has been going on for more than a year, and the decision between war and peace is uncertain. The cowardly naturally become depressed, and the strong naturally become indignant. As a result, opinions are noisy and do not agree with each other. Since there is no unified position, there is no concentrated strength. The entire nation is scattered like sand. Therefore, the current way to remedy this is to accept the demands of the majority of the people and decide on a major policy towards foreign countries. Only by having a firm position towards foreign countries can we make the people's hearts have something to rely on, can we stop the noise of parties and factions, can we rectify the abandoned discipline, and can we establish a central force. Otherwise, internal pacification will never be possible, and external aggression will never be possible. This is one explanation.

Secondly, the fact that our country is full of bandits and the people cannot make a living is also a prominent issue. However, the reason why bandits are rampant is precisely the inevitable result of the aggression of the great powers against China for decades. The trade deficit of 300 million taels of customs silver in ten years is the direct result of imperialism's aggression against China. The loss of 100 million yuan in civil war in twenty years is the indirect result of imperialism's aggression against China. The current collapse of the rural economy is the sum of imperialist aggression. And the bandits who take the risk are precisely the inevitable product of rural bankruptcy. Therefore, even from the point of view of pacifying bandits, repelling foreign aggression comes first. Only by repelling foreign aggression can we block the armed aggression of imperialists, and only by repelling foreign aggression can we block the economic exploitation of imperialists. The way to save the countryside is here. The way to stabilize people's livelihood is also here. If we fail to stop the aggression of imperialism and only use high pressure to suppress the hungry and cold [bandits], then the countryside will decline day by day, and the people will have nowhere to die. Those who take the risk will hardly not become bandits. In that case, when will internal pacification be possible, and when will external aggression be possible? This is another explanation.

Our nation has been dominated by the iron hooves of imperialists for a hundred years. And the talk of great powers redividing the world and preparing for a second world war is even more like madness. The outbreak of the September 18th Incident is also a prelude to the Second World War. Therefore, if our nation still cannot recognize the great disaster facing us today and cannot concentrate the full strength of our nation to wage a war to the death with Japanese imperialism, but only painstakingly strives for internal pacification, it is only clearing obstacles for imperialists to sweep away investments. Therefore, when we weigh the priorities, under the current circumstances, we believe that internal pacification must come before repelling foreign aggression. Those who advocate the theory of [internal pacification to repel foreign aggression] today only want to use it to cover up their cowardice.

East Bank of the Shi River

Enemy Troops Charge Our Positions 27

Our Troops Resisted Forcefully for Two Hours Before the Enemy Began to Retreat

The Weather in Qinyu Reaches Minus Twenty Degrees Celsius

Japanese Troops in Yuguan Dig Trenches for More Than Thirty Li

Righteous Army Engages in Fierce Fighting with Puppet Troops in Yong'an Fort

(Beiping) On the morning of the 19th, around 8 AM, the enemy troops on the east bank of the Shi River increased by about 1,400. At 10 AM, more than 500 enemy troops, using tanks as cover, charged our positions. A certain regiment of our army fiercely resisted. After holding out for two hours, the enemy began to retreat towards the west gate of Yuguan. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) There is no fighting on the Shi River front line. Qinbu is peaceful. There is still artillery fire at Jiukou, but it is small-scale contact with no major battles. In the Yuguan area, there has been heavy snow and extreme cold for days. The enemy has built fortifications in Yuguan, extending west from Tianzhuang, Tucheng, and Shihe Bridge, and north from Erdaogou to Erlangmiao Jiaoshan, digging trenches for more than thirty li and building solid forts. All the materials from the Beining Railway Iron Factory have been secretly transported away to be used for constructing fortifications. A certain unit of the Righteous Army is engaged in fierce fighting with the troops of Zhang Bi's puppet Jingguo Army in Yong'an Fort. The enemy sent three planes to bomb, but the enemy planes left after being fired upon by the Righteous Army using anti-aircraft machine guns. The Righteous Army is still engaged in fierce fighting with the puppet troops in the Yong'an Fort area. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Shi River front line and Qinhuangdao have been very calm for days. Japanese warships in Qinhuangdao come and go unpredictably, sometimes increasing and sometimes decreasing. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Japanese garrison stationed in Qinhuangdao has been sending six armed soldiers to guard the station since the 17th. They use the Boxer Protocol as protection, and we have no way to stop them. Their intention is that when necessary, they can first destroy our transportation facilities. Chinese banks such as Jiaotong Bank, Hebei Industrial Bank, etc., have already transported their money and accounts to Tianjin for business. The area south of the railway in that area is designated as a warning line for the Kailuan Mining Bureau, with British naval landing troops on patrol and guard. There was no fighting in Shimen and Shihe on the 19th.

(Nanjing) He Zhuguo telegraphed a certain important person, saying that our garrison is restricted by the Boxer Protocol. The Japanese soldiers are in a position to attack from both inside and outside, and the disparity in numbers is too great. We have no choice but to retreat in pain, and he is extremely excited, with a grand vow as if he would not return to life if he did not recover the lost land. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The weather in Qinyu today is extremely cold, reaching minus twenty degrees Celsius, which has not been seen in recent years. Many soldiers have had their ears and noses frozen off and have been sent to Tangshan Hospital for treatment. He Zhuguo personally went to the front to inspect and encourage the morale of the troops. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Many Japanese cavalry have been discovered in Yuguan City today. There is only one regiment of enemy troops from Yuguan to the Shi River. The Japanese headquarters is now in Chaoyang. It is said that there are six or seven divisions of Japanese troops stationed in that area. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) After the Japanese army occupied Yuguan, Yoshioka, a staff officer representing the commander of the Kwantung Army, arrived in Yuguan from Jinzhou on the 15th and met with Brigade Commander Suzuki. Suzuki has been appointed as the Yuguan Border Guard Commander and has posted notices in the cities and villages, indicating that the Japanese army in Yuguan intends to spy westward. (19th Special Dispatch)

To Secure Various Counties in Heilongjiang Province 28

(Beiping) In the various counties of Heilongjiang Province, the Japanese side is recruiting puppet military police to form local security general teams. Envoys From Various Countries Postpone Entry to Beijing 37

Sino-Japanese Disputes...

British Envoy Willing to Mediate

Subsequently, due to the Yuguan Incident and the continuous increase of Japanese troops, the interests of various countries in North China will obviously be affected. Therefore, French Envoy Wilden and American Envoy Johnson were unable to come to Beijing for a time. On the one hand, the interests of Britain and France in China will not be affected. After Envoy Lampson arrives in Beijing, the envoys from the United States, France, and Italy will come to Beijing to discuss. (19th Special Dispatch)

At the Next Central Political Council Meeting

The Provincial Governor System May Be Decided 38

(Nanjing) At the Third Plenary Session, Central Committee member Shi Ying and others proposed to change the chairman of the provincial government to a provincial governor system. The Central Political Council then discussed it and fully agreed with the principle of this establishment. It was handed over to the Political Report Group for further review, and two most important points were raised: 1. The candidates for provincial governor must be appointed from among civil servants; 2. All military and political affairs under the provincial administration shall be under the jurisdiction of the provincial governor. In this way, provincial administration can be unified. It is now heard that this provincial administration establishment will be voted on at the next Central Political Council meeting. (19th Special Dispatch)

Unified National Treasury Conference

Discussions Have Not Yielded Results 39

(Nanjing) The Unified National Treasury Conference convened by the Ministry of Finance held its second meeting on the 19th. Representatives from various agencies reported the opinions of their respective heads of agencies on the case to the meeting one after another. After a long discussion, no decision was reached. It was decided to continue the meeting on the 20th to discuss. It is heard that the various agencies do not insist on opposing the unified method and principles, but they hope to set a transition method before implementation to take into account the factual problems. (19th Special Dispatch)

Ministry of Communications Changes

Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau System 42

(Nanjing) According to the Ministry of Communications, the problem of changing the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau system is that the Remittance Bureau will be subordinate to the Postal Administration and subject to its supervision, rather than abolishing the original bureaus and merging them into the post office. The Supervisory Committee of the Remittance Bureau must still exist. This plan is currently being studied item by item by the Ministry and the Postal Economic System Research Association. (19th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau believes that due to the sharp fall in the Japanese yen, various reciprocal insurance rates, such as parcel insurance, letter insurance, mailbox insurance, and remittance insurance, etc., for insurance amounts of 1,000 Japanese yen in the past, have now fallen. Since the insured amount is proportional to the value, if damage should unfortunately occur in the future, there will inevitably be a risk of compensation. Therefore, the highest insurance will be raised uniformly one month from now to compensate for the losses due to the fall in the Japanese yen. A telegram was sent to the Ministry of Culture yesterday reporting the reasons for the increase and requesting approval. (19th Special Dispatch)

Jinxi has fallen, Dongxiang has been looted, Chongren has been occupied, Linchuan is surrounded, and Nanchang is threatened. People's hearts are wavering. Furthermore, commercial associations and other groups telegraphed Chiang on the 15th, stating that eastern Jiangxi has become a haven for bandits. Chongren and Xuwan are firmly in their hands. Leping and Yugan are also suffering encirclement. Although heavy troops are stationed in Fujian, the bandit forces have not been weakened. The provincial capital is in shock. This is truly a matter of national survival. (18th Day Special Dispatch)

(Nanchang) Reports from the west bank of the Gan River indicate that the bandits have a "pseudo" Third Army Corps, a "pseudo" Eighth Army, a "pseudo" Independent Division, an Independent Regiment, and a "pseudo" Red Army School, along with defense bureaus in the provinces and counties, totaling 4,000 rifles. The "pseudo" Xiang-Gan Provincial Government is located in Yongxin, and the Agricultural and Workers Bank issues paper currency worth 10,000 yuan daily. The "pseudo" army numbers 20,000. Due to a lack of medicine, many are suffering from ulcers. The bandits have attacked Jinxi and Linchuan, suffering 8,000 casualties, and are forcing farmers to transport goods to the Ningdu area. Wu Heling Hosts Beijing Press 65

(Nanjing) Wu Heling of the Mongolian Affairs Office hosted the press, reporting that the telegram from ten Mongolian representatives opposing Shi Qingyang, Zhang Wen, and himself was inappropriate. He also stated that the Mongolian system consists of twenty leagues in Inner and Outer Mongolia, divided into 240 banners. Each league has a league leader, and each banner has a Jasal or Chief Administrator. Chief Administrators are hereditary and often hold princely titles, known as Banner-Managing Princes. Each banner also has untitled princes, known as Idle Princes. Outer Mongolia has already been communized. Only Inner Mongolia has eight leagues and four special banners, totaling 77 banners. Except for the eight banners of Hulunbuir and the eleven banners of Chahar and one special banner in Tumet, which are under the control of the Chief Administrator, the remaining six leagues and three special banners, totaling 56 banners, each have a Banner-Managing Prince, that is, one Jasal. The opinions expressed by idle princes and civilians, regardless of their importance, cannot represent the league or banner. (19th Day Special Dispatch)

World Economic Conference 83

May is Expected to be When it will be Convened

National News Agency, Geneva, 18th - The work of the preparatory committee for the World Economic Conference is now nearing completion, so all parties are free to discuss its recommendations. The draft resolution jointly prepared by the American representative, Mr. Tan, and the Italian representative, Mr. Benidusi, is worded earnestly and movingly. The most important point is that the number of unemployed workers worldwide has reached 30 million. This number may be underestimated, as it should be at least between 75 million and 90 million when counting the families of the unemployed. Furthermore, the high tariff barriers that have been implemented by various countries in the past three years are also a major cause of the current economic depression.

National News Agency, Geneva, 18th - It was learned tonight from reliable sources that the Monetary Sub-Committee of the World Economic Conference Preparatory Committee has already drafted a report and agreed to the American representative's request to delete all language relating to war debts. This report has been sent to the drafting committee, which will be incorporated into the general report and submitted to the General Assembly of Experts tomorrow. Now that the American representative's request has been met, the obstacles to American participation have been removed, and it is expected that the World Economic Conference can be convened in May, and the notice of the meeting can be issued before the end of this month.

Havas News Agency, Geneva, 19th - The Economic Conference Preparatory Committee will hold a general meeting in the evening to adopt the general report drafted by the Economic and Monetary Sub-Committees. The summary of the Preparatory Committee's formal work report will be published in the evening. The preface to the general report was drafted by Mr. Yu, an American observer. Regarding the war debt issue in the preface, it is stated that the experts hope that the countries concerned will take appropriate measures to resolve intergovernmental debts, which are hindering the recovery of the world's economy and finance, and that countries will cooperate closely.

US Constitutional Amendment 84

President and Congressional Terms Moved Up

Reuters, Washington, 18th - The constitutional amendment passed by Congress changing the terms of the President and Congressmen has been ratified by 26 states. Now it is short of 10 states to reach the required number. When 36 states have ratified it and the ratifications are recorded by the Secretary of State, the amendment to the constitution will be announced and will take effect on October 15th. The amendment stipulates that the new Congress will take office on January 3rd after each general election, so that the defeated representatives can step down. The terms of the President and Vice President will both begin on January 20th.

US Government Fails to Raise Taxes 85

National News Agency, Washington, 18th - Today, the Democratic members of the House Ways and Means Committee secretly decided that all new tax bills would be left to a special session to be convened after the new President takes office on March 4th. Therefore, the hope of creating a new tax to balance the budget during the Republican government's term has been dashed, as the party still opposes a universal sales tax. Swiss Priest Goes to Tibet

Building New Himalayan Temple 86

Using Dogs to Rescue Lost Travelers

National News Agency, Geneva, January 18 - Two priests from the famous St. Bernard Monastery, Mr. Merai and Mr. Kegu, accompanied by two companions, are heading to the Layin Pass in Tibet, which is 12,000 feet high, with the intention of building a new temple there and carrying out the traditional work of rescuing lost travelers with dogs. This work has been carried out in Switzerland for many years, but with the advancement of Swiss civilization, dozens of cars pass through the St. Bernard Pass, even in winter, so it is no longer needed. The new Himalayan temple is expected to be completed in three years, at which time all the people and dogs of the St. Bernard Monastery will move there.

French Government Still Facing Difficulties 87

National News Agency, Paris, 19th - After discussing Finance Minister Cheron's rigorous plan to balance the budget, the House Finance Committee decided to consider the Socialist Party's counter-proposal as a basis for a compromise. Cheron's opposition was ineffective. Today's morning newspapers all said that if the cabinet continues to support Cheron's plan, it may not avoid collapse, as the Radical Socialists also have significantly different opinions on the cabinet's proposals. Moreover, public resentment is now erupting, and students at various industrial schools have decided to declare a 48-hour strike as a sign of opposition to Cheron.

Hitler and Papen Meet 88

Failure to Restore Nationalist Front Line

National News Agency, Berlin, 18th - Papen and Hitler met today, with important leaders of the National Socialist Party in attendance. The content of the talks was kept strictly secret, but political circles claimed tonight that Papen's attempt to restore the United Front of Nationalists had definitively failed, and for a time it did not seem that the National Socialist leaders would meet with the Federal Counselor either. It is expected that the Standing Committee of the National Assembly will finally pass the resolution on Friday to convene the National Assembly on January 24th, and conflicts may occur between the government and the National Assembly in the future, leading to the dissolution of the National Assembly.

Repercussions of Philippine Independence 89

National News Agency, Washington, 18th - Senators opposing Philippine independence are currently studying ways to prevent the implementation of the plan on the grounds that it is unconstitutional. However, since the constitution stipulates that Congress has the power to dispose of American territories and other property, legal experts have contributed very little opinion on this. According to news from the Philippines, the island's Legislative Assembly does not seem to be very much in favor of this plan, and it may not be eager to formulate a Philippine constitution. According to the provisions of the plan, Filipinos must formulate a constitution and submit it to the American President for approval within two years after the plan is approved. Therefore, even if Filipinos are restricted from formulating a constitution, if the American President is determined to prevent independence, it is very easy to do so: he only needs to refuse to approve the constitution, raise objections, and return it to the Philippines to be amended. Because the Philippine Legislature has no power to overturn the President's veto, this kind of rejection and amendment can often lead to indefinite delays.

National News Agency, Newtown Square, 18th - General Butler, known for his outspokenness, has been silent on current affairs for two months. He released his opinion on Philippine independence today, saying that after Philippine independence, it will become part of the Japanese Empire within two years. However, he does not therefore oppose Congress passing the independence bill, as he believes that Filipinos should be given freedom, as the island is of no benefit to the United States, and will only lead the United States into Asian wars. The Washington Conference Treaty prevented the United States from building fortress projects in the Philippines, and the island's current defense situation cannot withstand a genuine attack.

National News Agency, New York, 18th - Today's New York Tribune attacked the US Congress for passing the Philippine independence bill, hoping that Filipinos would refuse to accept it, and criticizing Congress for disregarding national honor, not thinking about national business, and ignoring its obligations to Filipinos. It does not know what its intention is and is opening this absurd historical move of removing the American flag.

Philippine Student Congress

Celebrating the Establishment of Independence 90

Reuters, Manila, 18th - Students here held a congress today to celebrate the establishment of the Philippine independence bill in the American Congress, while Philippine legislators have unofficially discussed whether to accept or reject the plan. The President of the Philippine Senate, Yu Song, has not commented to the local newspapers, but said that he believes that the future Democratic Congress will definitely approve the plan.

Russo-Japanese Non-Aggression Treaty

Negotiations Unsuccessful, Disputes Have Arisen 91

Electric News Agency, Tokyo, 19th - Vice-Minister Arida invited the Soviet Ambassador, Torayanavsky, to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at noon.
