40-Hour Work Week 95

The Kokumin News Agency, Geneva, 18th – The governments of Germany, Italy, France, Belgium, the Netherlands, Spain, Chile, and other countries jointly submitted a proposal to the International Labour Conference today, supporting the proposal for a 40-hour work week, stating that it is currently the only way

to alleviate unemployment. However, they also noted that attention should be paid to the daily lives of workers to ensure that they can maintain their normal standards. Furthermore, trade unions have also proposed that wages should not be reduced as a result of reduced working hours, and that the working hours of agricultural workers should be reduced equally. These demands are strongly opposed by employers. Therefore, the proposals of the governments of Germany, Italy, France, Belgium, and other countries are not without conflict with those proposed by the trade unions.

Japan's 1933 War Budget (Continued) (Japan News Agency) 96

Militaristic Policy and Preparing to Attack Russia

Swelling Expenditures and Financial Crisis

Financial Crisis and the Situation of Struggle

The Struggle of the Laboring Masses and the Limits of Financial Expansion 97

The expenditures in the 1933 budget had already been decided at 2.2 billion, but in October 1932, each department submitted a new demand totaling 2.9 billion, most of which was for war purposes. Although each department was making endless requests, the Ministry of Finance reduced the total to 2.2 billion. However, Army Minister Araki said, "At a time when the nation is facing a crisis of survival, should we be stingy with five or ten million yen?" As a result, another 100 million was added. Finance Minister Takahashi, having no other choice, had to issue new public bonds without limit. The increased issuance of public bonds caused inflation and rising prices, directly impacting the lives of the masses. The interest on the increased issuance of public bonds directly exploited the blood and sweat of the masses, shaking the stability of society. The broad masses of laborers fell into blatant poverty, unable to pay rent and land taxes. Therefore, the government allowed the payment of local fees in kind (even with payment in kind), but most people were still unable to pay. However, the government continued to demand payment, even stripping away anything of slight value. This shows that the root of the problem lies in the poverty of the masses.

The Financial Crisis Does Not Harm the Private Enrichment of the Zaibatsu 98

All financial policies adopted to alleviate the financial crisis or to alleviate the panic caused by the financial crisis do not hinder the private enrichment of a small number of monopolistic capitalists in the slightest. On the contrary, the former can make the latter even richer, while also deepening the crisis. Taking this year's budget as an example, the military expenses (Manchurian Incident expenses and military equipment improvement expenses) are nothing more than a huge profit for the monopolistic state capital and the large zaibatsu such as Mitsui and Mitsubishi. They use intensive labor and low wages to desperately squeeze and exploit workers. The relief fund, that is, the business expenses for military civil engineering projects, is also transferred to the hands of monopolistic large capitalists due to the purchase of timber

Page 8

and metal raw materials. Finally, the public bond expenses will further contribute a few interest payments to those financial capitalists. On the contrary, small and medium-sized enterprises have declined, and the laboring masses are still working desperately until they are shattered to pieces. As a result, class antagonism has become increasingly fierce and acute. In fact, the intensification of monopoly capital has long been a characteristic of the collapse of the capitalist system.

The Ineffectiveness of Unemployment Relief and the Situation of Struggle 99

Finally, regarding the relief of the 3.5 million unemployed, the government, in order to avoid the shaking of its own position, knows that it must provide a minimum level of relief for the struggle of the unemployed. However, this small amount of false benevolence cannot be achieved due to the financial crisis. This is the basic contradiction of the current wartime finance. The number of unemployed people is increasing, the state of starvation is worsening day by day, and the poverty of the laboring masses is deepening. However, they do not receive any subsidies or improved treatment from the government. Today, the united struggle of workers and farmers among the unemployed masses will inevitably become acute. And the financial crisis is precisely promoting the development of this situation of struggle. (Posted from Tokyo on January 10th)

The Northeast Problem and the League of Nations (15)

Spanish Representative Reprimands Matsuoka 100

The Spanish representative, Mr. Madariaga, said, "I fully agree with the opinion expressed by the Czech representative. It is my understanding that the Japanese representative may have misunderstood the procedures for discussing matters in the Council due to a lack of experience. The Japanese representative hopes that the meeting will not be prolonged, and this is our common hope. He also stated that if the members of the Council were to ask the chairman of the Commission of Enquiry for his opinion, the Council's session might be extended. He further stated that, according to the terms of reference of the Commission of Enquiry, the Council's appointment of the Commission was to request it to conduct an on-site investigation and report its findings to the Council. I fully agree that we should fully comply with the provisions of this term of reference. However, I have also carefully studied the section submitted by the Japanese representative and found that it does not contain any provision stating that the Chairman or members of the Council may not ask the Commission of Enquiry for its opinion on the report it has produced. We already have the report of the Commission of Enquiry on its on-site investigation. However, upon close examination of the terms of reference of the Commission, it does not specifically designate any one report. The Commission has already produced a preliminary report, so it would not be inappropriate for the Council to request the Commission to produce a further report if necessary. Therefore, I believe that the Council may well ask the Commission whether, after hearing the opinions of both sides here, it intends to change the report of its investigation on the ground. The report of the Commission of Enquiry is highly commendable, but although its evidence is extremely substantial, it is possible that not all of the Commission's findings have been included in the report, or that members of the Council still need to know these facts, which can only be ascertained by questioning the Commission in person. This is undoubtedly entirely appropriate. As to whether the Commission still exists at this time, I believe that there is no need for further discussion. The Commission was appointed by the Council and is one of its organs, but at the same time, the Commission has become one of the organs of the Assembly of the League of Nations. Therefore, I firmly believe that the Assembly of the League of Nations will not wish the Commission to be dissolved before it has considered the facts contained in the report. Therefore, there is no doubt that the Commission still exists and that the Council may consult it at any time. Moreover, the continued existence of the Commission provides the Council with many opportunities, and it would be very unwise of us to neglect this opportunity. In short, the Commission continues to exist and its services are still available to the Council. Therefore, if the Council deems it necessary, it may ask for its opinion on any point. If the meeting time is extended as a result, it is unavoidable. Furthermore, the discussion of this case has already been extended for more than a year, and it is unlikely that extending it by another month would be a matter of the utmost importance."

Drummond Cites Two Precedents 101

Sir Eric Drummond, Secretary-General, said that it was customary for commissions of enquiry appointed by the League of Nations to be brought to Geneva to be directed by the Council without exception. For example, after the dispute between Greece and Bulgaria in 1925, a complaint was lodged with the League of Nations in accordance with Article 11 of the Covenant. The Commission of Enquiry appointed by the League of Nations, chaired by Sir Horace Rumbold, also attended the Council meeting in December 1925. The last section of the terms of reference of the Commission stated that,

(The Commission shall conduct investigations on the ground and in the capitals of the two governments concerned, and the two governments shall provide the Commission with all assistance, provide all facilities, and take the necessary steps to enable it to complete its work.)

On this point, while the Council was considering the report, Sir Austen Chamberlain, who had submitted the case, proposed to ask the governments of Bulgaria and Greece if they had any comments to make. After the motion was passed, Sir Austen Chamberlain further suggested that the Chairman of the Commission be asked to indicate whether there was anything further to add. This is one example. There is also another example, namely the case of Mosul. When this matter occurred, the Council also appointed a Commission of Enquiry, chaired by General Laidoner, to prepare a report on the provisional border between Turkey and Iraq and submit it to the Council. General Laidoner also attended the Council meeting and provided any additional comments required by the Council at any time. The above two commissions of enquiry were both extremely important. Therefore, the procedures followed show the usual practice of the Council. There are also other similar examples, which I will present one by one if the members of the Council are interested.

British Representative Expresses Opinion 102

Sir John Simon, the British representative, said, "Mr. Chairman, I have been hesitant to express my views when you have asked for opinions, as many of those present at the Council have more experience than I do. I believe that after listening to the statements of the Czech and Spanish representatives, we should all be very impressed, as both gentlemen have many years of experience with the Council's procedures. Moreover, the two precedents cited by the Secretary-General are sufficient to prove the truth of this practice, and there is no need for me to say more. I would like to speak on one point of fact. The five members of the Commission of Enquiry have in fact been present at the Council meetings this week. Their presence here is not without cause, and it is not merely to observe or listen, but in fact they have been invited here by the League of Nations and its organs to do useful work. I ask, what other work is there than to help the Council in its deliberations, as you have proposed?"

Matsuoka Resorts to Written Statement After Running Out of Arguments 103

[Matsuoka:] "I am really unwilling to debate this matter further, but judging from the two matters raised by the Secretary-General, it seems that our views are still being misunderstood. We do not object to the members of the Commission of Enquiry explaining any section of the report to the representatives of the Council, or adding anything to the report, nor have we expressed any opposition. However, we must raise an objection in principle, not in procedure, to the Commission of Enquiry taking the Council's deliberations into account and expressing its opinions on the Council's deliberations, as any expression of opinion by the Council should come entirely from the Council and not from any other organ. We do not object in any way to the Commission of Enquiry explaining or adding to any part of the report, but judging from what you have said, it seems to include what we have been considering here for the past few days, as well as the statement submitted by Japan. This is a matter of principle, and we oppose it. I respectfully request that you give us an opportunity to present our arguments in writing."

(Chairman:) "I think the difficulty of this matter lies only in the form of the question. This matter can be easily resolved once the Chairman of the Commission of Enquiry arrives. Are you satisfied with this, Japanese representative?"

(Matsuoka:) "Yes."

(Chairman:) "I believe that the Council is very willing to receive the written opinion of the Japanese representative, and I personally am very eager to see it first. At the same time, I believe that the members of the Council have no objection to asking the Commission of Enquiry to consider whether there is anything to add to or subtract from its report. (No objections from the members)"

Debate on the Afternoon of the 25th

Japan's Official Letter Opposing the Commission of Enquiry 104

The Chairman said, "I have just received an official letter from the Japanese representative. I will now read its contents to the representatives of the Council.

[Mr. Chairman, In accordance with the understanding reached at the Council meeting yesterday, I have drafted a memorandum on the views of the Japanese delegation regarding the work of the Commission of Enquiry appointed by the Council resolution of December 10, 1931, and its authority at this Council meeting, and submit it herewith for your consideration. Respectfully, Yosuke Matsuoka, Japanese Representative to the Council.

(1) The work of the Commission of Enquiry appointed by the Council on December 10, 1931, is completed from the date the report is submitted to the Council.

(2) The Japanese delegation does not object to the members of the Commission of Enquiry now in Geneva, individually or collectively, providing the Council with explanations of the content of the report upon request. The Japanese delegation also does not object to the Commission adding to or subtracting from the report if it deems it necessary. However, it should be made clear that the explanations provided by the Commission should only relate to those sections of the report that are not clear and definitive, and that any additions or subtractions should only be limited to the reconsideration or re-examination of the report itself and the information obtained by the Commission during its on-site investigation, and not to anything else.

(3) Japan cannot recognize the right of the members of the Commission of Enquiry to express opinions or criticisms on the statement submitted by the Japanese government to the Council, or on the statements made by the Japanese representative on the Council floor from the start of the meeting last Monday.

(4) If the Chairman's original proposal, which is to ask the Commission to consider whether to change its opinion in view of the statements made by the Chinese and Japanese sides, is accepted, then the Japanese representative will inevitably have to question the members of the Commission in order to defend the Japanese government to the League of Nations. Once this questioning begins, it will take a very long time. This is what the Japanese representative is most eager to avoid. The Japanese representative's objection to the Chairman's original proposal is for this reason. One]

The Council has read the Japanese representative's official letter. The Chairman then invited Lord Lytton, Chairman of the Commission of Enquiry, to attend and said, "Before I ask the representatives of the Council if they have any questions to ask the members of the Commission of Enquiry, I would like to ask the Chairman of the Commission first if the Commission has anything to add to or subtract from its report."

Lord Lytton's Reply 105

Lord Lytton said, "[Mr. Chairman, Ladies and Gentlemen, I humbly follow the request of my colleagues and express my gratitude to you and the representatives of China and Japan for your appreciation of our work. If our report can ultimately prove helpful to the League of Nations in considering this extremely complicated and difficult matter, then our efforts will have been well worth it. Other than that, we have nothing else to say.]"

The Chairman Asks for the Opinions of the Representatives 106

The Chairman said, "[The representatives of the Council have heard the reply of the Chairman of the Commission of Enquiry. Do any of the representatives have any questions to ask the Commission of Enquiry regarding any section of the report? (No one responds) Then none of the representatives of the Council wish to ask any questions of the Commission of Enquiry? (No one responds) In that case, do any of the representatives of the Council wish to discuss the report or raise any points?]"

Czech Representative Expresses Opinion 107

The Czech representative, Mr. Benes, said, "[Mr. Chairman, I am speaking at this time on the issue before the Council or on the report itself, as I reserved the right to speak and explain my views in the Council when this case was placed on the Council's agenda. However, in recent days, there have been significant developments in this case, and judging from the opinions of some of my colleagues, it seems that the simplest solution to this case would be to submit the entire case to the Assembly for discussion. The Assembly has the right to deal with the entire issue in accordance with Article 15 of the Covenant. I believe that you will also make this suggestion, so I will not express my opinion on this case at this time, so as to avoid duplication in the Assembly. However, I will certainly express my opinion when the Assembly meets.]"

The Chairman's Hope for Both Sides 108

The Chairman said, "[Are there any other representatives of the Council who wish to speak? (No one responds) The representatives of China and Japan have both expressed their opinions on the Lytton Report. Therefore, the question before the Council is whether to further delay the submission of this matter to the Special Assembly, in accordance with the request contained in the Assembly's resolution of March 11. The Council passed a resolution on February 19 to submit this case to the Assembly for handling in accordance with Article 15, paragraph 9 of the Covenant. Therefore, the Assembly has acquired the entire case and has the direct responsibility to seek a solution. I stated at the meeting on September 24 that our transfer of this case to the Assembly does not reduce the Council's freedom to decide whether to discuss this report, as this report is based on another article of the Covenant of the League of Nations. However, I believe that it is entirely in line with the Council's resolution of February 19 to submit this case to the Assembly not to start a comprehensive discussion after hearing the opinions of China and Japan. If we have important and practical considerations that can be grounds for discussing this matter in the Council, then we may as well proceed with the discussion. However, based on the current facts, this practical consideration lies there and not here. Therefore, I believe that we all hope that the Special Assembly can discuss this case at the earliest possible date. The representatives of the Council are also the representatives of the Assembly, so they will have the opportunity to participate in everything in the Assembly in the future and can express their opinions in the organ responsible for resolving this case. I myself also have opinions to express on the report of the Commission of Enquiry, and I firmly believe that the position of the other representatives of the Council is the same as mine. After this case is handed over to the Assembly, we will still have the opportunity to express our opinions, and for the reasons I have stated, it is more appropriate for our opinions to be expressed in the Assembly meeting than in the Council meeting. Moreover, I cannot help but say that when I listened carefully to the speeches of the Chinese and Japanese representatives, I and the other members of the Council paid the most attention to whether there was anything in the words of both sides that could make us believe that there was a satisfactory and swift solution ahead. This case has been delayed for quite some time and should be resolved as soon as possible. However, judging from the speeches of both sides, there is not enough to arouse our optimism. The Japanese government, in its statement, did not express acceptance of the principles of settlement recommended by the Commission, except for the negative phrase "restoring the status quo is not a solution." The Chinese delegation, on the other hand, stated that it reserved the right to present its views on the terms of settlement in the future, and currently only agreed to the third of the ten principles listed in the Commission's report, namely "any settlement should be in accordance with the provisions of the Covenant of the League of Nations, the Kellogg-Briand Pact, and the Washington Nine-Power Treaty." Judging from the above, it seems that China and Japan have not yet reached any agreement on what is recommended in the report, which the Council can cite as a basis or recommendation as a practical aid when the Special Assembly decides on a solution. As the Chairman of the Council, I cannot help but express the hope that the opinions expressed by the Chinese and Japanese representatives in the past few days do not represent the final positions of the Chinese and Japanese governments. If a method is provided that offers the possibility of a fair and lasting solution to this tragic dispute, it is hoped that it will not be rejected by either China or Japan. I believe that what I am saying now can not only represent the Council, but also represent the public opinion of the whole world. It should be known that we now have this League of Nations and its organs for the peaceful resolution of disputes such as the one before us, thanks to the fact that world public opinion after the Great War abhorred war. If two member states of the League, as important as China and Japan, once a dispute arises and cannot make full use of the power of the League, or if one of the two parties to the dispute refuses to cooperate, causing the proceedings of the League's organs to be obstructed, then it is tantamount to showing contempt for world public opinion, which is absolutely intolerable. Therefore, I would like to represent the Council in earnestly requesting both representatives, after expressing their opinions, to shift their attention to the practical aspects of this case and to sincerely consider how to assist the League of Nations in seeking a solution."

[Matsuoka:] "If the Chinese representative wishes to speak before me, please speak first."

[Gu:] "Please allow me to speak later."

Important Meeting on the Situation in Southwest China Held 109

Li Zongren and Representatives from Various Provinces Attend

Resolutions on Southwest China's National Defense Preparations and Other Issues

Guangzhou Correspondence: Li Zongren, Commander-in-Chief of the Fourth Army Group, recently came to Guangzhou from Nanning in light of the fall of Yuquan and the increasingly urgent national crisis. He is here to discuss countermeasures with military authorities and Central Committee members from various regions. He arrived in Guangzhou at 10 a.m. on the 11th, accompanied by his wife, Guo Dejie. Those traveling with him included Dan Maoxin, representative from Yunnan Province; Gan Jiayi, special inspector from the Southwest Political Committee in Guizhou Province; Liang Chaoji, adjutant of the Seventh Army in Guangxi Province; and Ma Junwu, President of Guangxi University. According to Li, "This trip to Guangzhou is purely to discuss how to deal with the serious situation in North China with the authorities in Southwest China. All sectors of Guangxi Province are filled with grief and indignation over the loss of Yuquan. Whether to send troops north will be decided after consultation with the Southwest Central Committee members. After recent rectifications in Guangxi, a small portion of the troops have been reduced, and we are now starting to work on construction. The war in Guizhou has been suspended for a long time. Wang Jialie's troops are currently stationed in Rongjiang, and there have been no reports of a counterattack on Guiyang. It seems that the situation in Guizhou can be said to be over for the time being." Li rested briefly at his private residence in Ma Penggang that day. That evening, he had a banquet at Tuisi Garden in Dongshan, where he discussed important public affairs concerning the current situation with Central Committee members from Southwest China. At 3 p.m. on the 12th, the Southwest Political Affairs Committee officially convened a meeting. Li Zongren, Tang Shaoyi, and others attended, and summoned representatives from various provinces. Those present included Dan Maoxin, Zhang Chong, Gan Fengzhang, Zhang Zhen'ou, envoy from Southwest China to Yunnan; Gan Jiayi, envoy from Southwest China to Guizhou; Yang Qiufan, representative from Guizhou; Wang Jianping, representative of Feng Yuxiang; He Minhun, Chairman of the Anti-Japanese Military Commission in Rehe; Jin Zishou and Liu Hanchuan, representatives from Hebei; Dai Jingyuan, representative from Hunan Province; Zhang Mingjiu, representative from Sichuan Province; Zhao Yijian, Chief of Staff of the 19th Route Army; and Chen Xiaohou, representative. The Southwest Political Affairs Committee members in attendance included Chen Jitang, Zou Lu, Deng Zheru, Liu Luyin, Liu Jiwen, Lin Yun, Chen Rong, Zhang Renmin, Li Xiangen, and Yang Xiji. At 3:30 p.m.,

the meeting began to discuss various issues. Representatives from all parties presented their opinions and reported on the recent situation in their respective areas. Apart from important matters that were inconvenient to disclose, Chen Jitang and Zou Lu later raised the issue of Southwest China's national defense preparations. The representatives had mutual discussions and resolved: (1) To adhere to the principle of resisting Japan and saving the nation, and to carry out everything in accordance with the telegram issued by the Political Affairs Committee on the fish day. (2) To urge the Central Government to implement the resolutions of the Third Plenary Session, to be determined to resist Japan,

to send troops to kill the enemy and recover the lost territories as soon as possible. (3) To strengthen the deployment of national defense in Southwest China by various provinces. (4) To resolve to provide long-term assistance to the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army. On that day, there were also discussions on the construction of the Qin-Yu Five-Province Railway and the economic construction of Southwest China, but no results were reached. The meeting adjourned at around 4 p.m. (January 13th)

Shandong Assists Central Government's Military Expenses Case

Wang Xiangrong to Report on Financial Situation in Beijing 110

Jinan Correspondence: When Liu Zhennian's troops were stationed in Shandong, the provincial government was responsible for a portion of the military pay for that division. Since that division was transferred to Zhejiang and Fujian, Shandong's assistance with military pay naturally ceased. Recently, the central government reached an agreement with the Shandong provincial government that, due to the central government's financial difficulties, the Shandong provincial government would assist the central government with 100,000 yuan per month. This has been approved by the provincial government and implemented starting in February. However, Shandong is impoverished and local finances are insufficient. In the future, regarding the matter of assisting the central government with 100,000 yuan, it may be necessary to find other ways to handle it. Therefore, Wang Xiangrong, the Director of the Department of Finance, needs to discuss solutions with the central government regarding this issue and report the general situation of local revenue and expenditure in Shandong to Chairman Chiang and the Ministry of Finance. He left for Beijing by the Jinpu train this morning (the 17th). According to Wang's remarks before his departure, "I have repeatedly received telegrams from Chairman Chiang summoning me to Beijing to inquire about the financial situation in Shandong, and I am also eager to take this opportunity to report the revenue and expenditure of the province to the Ministry of Finance. I will stay in Beijing for about a week before returning to Jinan. Regarding the central government's order for Shandong to assist with military expenses of 100,000 yuan per month, it is appropriate for Shandong to assist the central government if Shandong's finances are sufficient. However, the province's finances are also very difficult, and it will be necessary to find other ways to accomplish this in the future. Last year, the local revenue and expenditure of this province were both more than 25 million yuan. Due to excessive military expenses, there was inevitably a slight deficit. After the transfer of Liu Zhennian's troops, the more than ten counties in Jiaodong returned to the jurisdiction of the provincial government. It is expected that revenue may increase, but these counties have been devastated and their vitality has not recovered. They are requesting exemptions from surcharges and all supplementary levies. It is still uncertain whether there will be an increase in revenue in the future." (17th)

The Songhang Case Reopens for Debate 111

Still No Result, Debate Scheduled to Continue

Songjiang Correspondence: The Songhang arrears case was previously debated to a conclusion by the county court on December 6th of last year, with a scheduled pronouncement on the 12th. The civil court announced that the plaintiff requested to withdraw the lawsuit against defendants Gu Jiaxuan and Zhu Hesun, and the remaining cases were regarded as withdrawn with the plaintiff bearing the litigation costs. Afterwards, the creditors immediately applied for an interpretation. On December 26th, after the court served the ruling, the creditors immediately filed an appeal. The court then revoked the original ruling and scheduled a reopening of the debate at 2 PM on the 18th of this month, as previously reported. Yesterday marked the date of the reopened debate. On the plaintiff's side, the creditor representative Bai Guanlan and the proxy lawyers Qu and Liu Zhimou arrived. On the defendant's side, only the proxy lawyer Sha Xunyi and the special proxy Tang Mingshi arrived. President Wang, accompanied by Secretary Li, presided over the hearing. First, they questioned creditor representative Bai Guanlan about the purpose of reopening the debate, and then asked whether the target of the lawsuit was the board of directors or the shareholders. Bai then stated the reasons for withdrawing the case against the two households. President Wang suddenly sternly questioned, "The target of the lawsuit must be clarified before the lawyers of both parties can debate." He further inquired about the amount of Bai Guanlan's claim, to which he replied 700 yuan, deposited in the name of the real estate company. The judge asked, "What is your position in the real estate company?" He replied, "Manager." The judge then said, "This proof is necessary. Although there was an agreement to organize the real estate company at that time, it was not yet established, and the account was only in an individual name." The lawyer then said, "The creditor representative, Bai Guanlan, also registered the debt with the liquidator and has appeared in court several times, so there should be no doubt. Today, the court is hearing this case, and the situation is lively, but our proxy still asks the court to conduct the hearing with the same calm and impartiality as before. The interested parties should state the facts, and the law should supplement them. The court can direct the process regarding the litigation qualification at any time. In short, the opposing proxy will do everything possible to seek a quick resolution to this case." The judge then said, "There are two points to be addressed before reopening the debate in this case: 1) Creditor representative Bai Guanlan must supplement the procedures for his position as manager of the Songjiang Real Estate Company; 2) Is the lawsuit against the board of directors or the shareholders?" Lawyer Qu then said, "The first point can be supplemented according to the law. As for the second point, the board of directors, supervisors, etc. should bear joint liability. The creditors filed an appeal, which has led to the reopening of the debate. According to Article 475 of the Civil Procedure Law, if the appeal is deemed reasonable, the original court can correct the original ruling; otherwise, your court should have transferred the case to the appellate court for handling earlier. Furthermore, your court can refer to the first half of the prosecutor's office's decision of non-prosecution of Zhang Xiaomei et al., which is not much different." Then, after hearing the arguments of both parties, the court ordered a continuation of the debate at a scheduled time and adjourned.

Wuxi 114

Rain and Snow Cover the Roads, Causing Fatal Falls. Wuxi County Has Experienced Continuous Heavy Snow and Rain, and the Roads Are Covered with Accumulated Snow and Frozen, Making Them Exceptionally Slippery. Passersby Are Falling One After Another, Leading to the Lament, "It's Impossible to Walk!" On the Morning of the Previous Day, Zhu Shouchang, a Partner at the Ruiji Flour Store Outside Sanli Bridge, North Gate (Age 37), Was Going from His Home Outside South Gate to Work at the Store. Unfortunately, While Passing the Eastern End of Dagong Bridge, He Accidentally Slipped and Fell to the Ground. Subsequently, a Neighbor, Mr. Zhu, Caught Sight of Him, Rushed to Tell His Wife, Who Hurried Over to Help Him. However, His Face Had Already Turned Green, and He Was Unconscious. He Was Immediately Carried Home, and a Doctor Was Called to Treat Him, but He Had Already Expired.

City and Township General Mobilization for Conscript Labor to Dredge Rivers 115

Due to the Scarcity of Rainfall Last Year, the River Water Became Shallow and Dried Up After Winter, Making Ship Navigation Extremely Difficult. Heavily Loaded Vessels Almost Couldn't Navigate. The County Government Decided to Take Advantage of This Period to Implement River Dredging. Yesterday, a River Dredging Committee Meeting Was Specially Held with the County Construction Bureau, the County and City Financial Property Office, and the District Chiefs of the Seventeen Districts. The Following Was Decided: 1) Dredge the Original Surveyed Shuang River, Nanxing Pond River, Zhihu Port, Ma Jiagang, Ling, Hibiscus Pond Great River, Zhihu Port, and Ma Gang Ports. The Total Cost of Building Materials Is 5,500 Silver Dollars. In Addition to the 1,500 Silver Dollars Collected by the Construction Bureau in January, the Remaining 4,000 Silver Dollars Will Be Borne by the Construction Bureau as Future Water Conservancy Expenses. 2) The Construction Bureau Should First Survey and Estimate the Expenses for Dredging the North-South Trunk Rivers in the Urban Area, and Then Let the Local Fund-Raising Method Be Used to Implement Dredging. Furthermore, the North Great Bridge River (i.e., Lotus Rong Bridge), Which Is an Important Route for the Suzhou-Changzhou Canal, Is Also Severely Silted. The Two Towns of Beitang and Daqiao Decided to Dredge It, and the County Construction Bureau Estimated That the Project Would Require 5,600 Silver Dollars. A Meeting Was Held with Various Industries at the County Chamber of Commerce Yesterday, and the Following Was Decided: 1) Immediately Submit a Request to the County Government to Issue a Notice to Inform All Canal Shipping Households to Pay Attention to Ship Navigation and to Announce It in the Newspaper; 2) Organize a River Dredging Engineering Committee, Appointing Xiao Jian, Director of the Bureau, District Chief Qian, Zhao Zixin, Miao Lianchen, Yang Hanxi, Cai Jian, Qian Sunqing, Chen Zhanru, Tao Yinful, Feng Yunxiang, Jiang Huanqing, Qian Weiqing, Xue Mingjian, Qin Xiangtao, and Zou Songfan as Committee Members; 3) The County Chamber of Commerce Should Invite Various Industries to Raise Donations; 4) The Rice and Bean South Goods Industries Should Each Fill Out a Check for 500 Silver Dollars; 5) It Was Decided That the Dam Would Be Built and Dredging Would Begin on the 26th of This Month, Which Is the First Day of the Lunar New Year, with a Deadline of One and a Half Months for Completion. Furthermore, the River Channels in the Qianqiao Area of the Fourth District of the County Are Important Routes for Yixing Transport and Are the Lifeline for Irrigation in Kaiyuan and Fuan Townships. District Chief Zhu Has Completed the Survey, and It Has Been Decided to Use the Construction Bureau to Begin Dredging Immediately.

Fan Tianhang Released on Bail and Returns to Wuxi 116

Fan Tianhang, a Staff Member of the County Party Headquarters in This County, Was Previously Ordered by the Suzhou-Songjiang Bandit Suppression Headquarters to Send Him to Suzhou from Wuxi, Claiming That Fan Was Suspected of Disloyalty. At That Time, the County Party Headquarters Sent a Letter and Telegram to Prove His Innocence and Submitted It to the Provincial Party Headquarters, Which Quickly Telegraphed the Headquarters to Release Him. Yesterday, After the Headquarters' Investigation Made It Clear That He Had Not Committed Any Criminal Acts, He Was Immediately Released on Bail and Returned to Wuxi.

Zhenjiang Traffic After the Heavy Snow 118

The heavy snow of the previous morning stopped only in the evening. The snow on the roads was six or seven inches deep. Many telephone and electric light lines were damaged by the snow. Craftsmen are repairing them overnight, and telephone service in the city was restored this morning. Due to the clearing of snow, the Zhenjiang-Yangzhou buses only resumed normal service on the afternoon of the 18th. The long-distance buses on the Jiangsu-Jurong road only made one round trip yesterday. The Beijing-Shanghai trains, both northbound and southbound, were delayed due to insufficient heating in the cold weather. Canal boats have been suspended for several days due to ice.

Jiangsu Province Rectifies Water Traffic 119

In Recent Years, Robberies of Small Steamships on the Yangtze River and Inland Rivers Have Been Heard of From Time to Time. Sometimes Bandits Are Discovered on Board in the Middle of the Journey, or Bandits Suddenly Board Ships in Remote Places to Rob. The Reason for This Is That Passengers on Small Steamships Are Not Strictly Checked When Boarding and Alighting, Which Allows Bandits to Sneak In and Repeatedly Commit Robberies. In Order to Punish and Prevent Such Incidents, the Jiangsu Provincial Government Has Instructed the Local Public Security Bureaus and Security Teams to Conscientiously Conduct Inspections. On the One Hand, Armed Police Officers Should Be Stationed on Each Small Steamship to Protect the Ship, So That Criminals Cannot Sneak In and the Public Order of Water Traffic Can Be Ensured. The Provincial Government Yesterday Ordered the Security Department to Take Measures to Maintain Order So That Travelers Can Be Safe. At the Same Time, It Will Consult with the Department of Civil Affairs to Draft Measures and Order the Implementation and Report for Filing. Tongchonghaiqi Military and Police Escort

Nantong 120

The County Magistrates and Military and Police of the Four Counties of Nantong, Chongming, Haimen, and Qidong Have Discussed and Decided on Escort Measures and Submitted Them to the Department of Civil Affairs for Review. They Have Now Received Instructions That Robbery of Sailing Vessels Endangers the Safety of Travelers. The Reported Discussion and Determination of Escort Measures for Tongchonghaiqi Is a Crucial Plan. The Four Attached Opinions Are Mostly Consistent. Approval Should Be Granted for Careful Determination Based on These Opinions. However, How Should the Duties Be Assigned to the Military and Police Along the Way, What Responsibilities Should Be Defined, and How Should the Prevention of Inspection Disputes and the Dispatch of Escort Military and Police Be Managed and Replaced? All of This Should Be Detailed in the Measures for Compliance. As for the Fundraising Expenses Mentioned in the Original Letter from the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association, What Is the Situation? The Report Did Not Clearly State This. How Should This Expense Be Raised? A Budget Should Be Drafted and Reported in Detail Along with the Established Measures, and the Inspection and Detective Measures Discussed by the Water Police District Department Should Be Investigated and Reported Together for Review and Compliance. Representatives of the Four Counties Are Scheduled to Meet in Nantong Again on the 20th to Carefully Determine and Implement Detailed Measures.

The County Government Interrogates the Pingchao Massacre 121

The Pingchao District Office Killed Four Villagers, Including Lin Koushan, for Collecting Defense Donations, Arousing Huge Storms. At 7 PM on the 18th, County Magistrate Zhang Summoned District Chief Wang Zhenchao, the Defense Corps Kang Shalian and the Corps Workers, and Chen Shuhang, the Village Head Who Caused the Donation Incident. As a Result, the Case Is Being Investigated by the Prosecutor's Office and Will Be Sent to the Court for Handling.

Bandits Are Rampant Again Amidst the Sound of Lunar New Year Drums

Mingguang 122

After Being Vigorously Suppressed by the 11th Cavalry Brigade, the Bandit Disaster in This County Gradually Subsided. For Several Months, Although It Was During the Winter Defense Period, It Was Still Peaceful. Unexpectedly, Amidst the Sound of Lunar New Year Drums, Banditry Has Risen Again. The Details Are Recorded Separately Below: 1) Chen Qizhong, a Resident Behind the East Street of This Town, Was Kidnapped on the Night of the 10th; 2) In the Wild Chicken Area of the North Township, Three People Were Shot and Killed on the 11th, Two Were Injured, and Four Guns Were Lost; 3) The Tangmian Village in the Northeast Township Was Attacked by Bandits on the Evening of the 12th. Chen Minghe, a Squad Leader of the Self-Defense Corps, Was Killed in Action, Three Residents Were Killed, and 15 People, Including Chen Ruyuan, Were Kidnapped; 4) Guiying and Xiaoyuying Villages in the Northeast Township Were Captured at the Same Time on the Afternoon of the 15th. Thirteen People, Including the Yu Surname, Were Taken Away, and All the Houses Were Destroyed. It Is Heard That There Are About 300 Bandits, All Coming from the North.

Two Cargo Ships Robbed En Route

Jiaxing 123

A cargo ship from Jiaxing to Liyang was traveling from Liyang to Jiaxing on the 15th when it passed the Qilihui area north of Wangjiangjing. Seven bandits, armed with weapons, ordered the ship to stop and robbed all the cargo and money, more than 700 yuan. Another cargo ship from Jiaxing to Haining was traveling past the Xiushui Bridge outside the South Gate on the night of the 17th when a bandit ship suddenly approached and ordered it to stop. They jumped into the ship and searched and robbed the cargo of cigarettes, salted meat, and other miscellaneous items. Subsequently, the Taiping Bridge Township Defense Corps seized a small boat, which contained cigarettes and other items. They handed over the boat, items, and a bandit named Shen Jinhuai to the First District Corps, which in turn sent them to the court for interrogation.

No One Is Handling the Aftermath After the Sinking of the Xunning Tai Wheel

Ningbo 124

The Xunning Tai Wheel, Sailing Between Ningbo and Taiwan, Sank in the Waters of Sanshantou, Zhenhai. More Than 300 Crew Members, Stewards, and Passengers Were Not Able to Escape. The Details Have Been Recorded in This Newspaper. It Is Now Known That Since the Sinking of the Wheel, a Large Number of Floating Corpses Have Been Discovered in the Waters Near Sanshantou. As of Noon on the 16th, More Than 20 Bodies Had Been Salvaged by Xinqitou Village, More Than 60 Bodies Had Been Salvaged by Daxie Village, More Than 70 Bodies Had Been Salvaged by Lingtoushan Village, and More Than 10 Bodies Had Been Salvaged by Peixigen Village. Female Bodies Accounted for 5% of the Bodies, and Among the Male Bodies Were Li Caiyun, the Manager of the Ningbo Huichang Iron Factory, and Chen Xingzhang, a Partner of the Shipu Yongyichang Credit Bureau. Because There Were Books and Business Cards on Their Bodies, They Could Be Identified and Have Been Claimed. There Are Also Two Other Male Bodies That Can Be Identified, and the Family Members of the Deceased Have Been Notified to Claim the Bodies. The Remaining Bodies Have No Identifying Objects on Their Bodies, and No Family Members of the Deceased Have Claimed Them. The Xinqitou Helifang Owner Has Shown Great Compassion and Notified the Coastal People to Reward 10 Yuan for Each Body Salvaged and Has Prepared a Large Number of Coffins to Temporarily Collect the Bodies to Wait for the Family Members of the Deceased to Claim Them. Floating Corpses Are Still Being Discovered at Sea. After the Incident, The Company in Ningbo Has Been Repeatedly Questioned by the Family Members of the Deceased and Has Been Asked to Find Ways to Handle the Aftermath. The Company Has Only Begun to Find Ways to Handle the Aftermath, and Since the Previous Day, It Has Closed the Company and All the Employees Have Fled.

Local News

Ma Zhanshan's Representative Hosted the Press Yesterday 128

Reporting on Ma Zhanshan's Journey into Russia

And the Arrival of the Heilongjiang Army on the Border of Jehol

Central News Agency: Wu Huanzhang, representative of General Ma Zhanshan, Chairman of Heilongjiang Province, and Jiang Songnian, Counselor of the Heilongjiang Provincial Government, hosted a press conference at Zhongshe on Weihaiwei Road at 3 PM yesterday. More than a dozen reporters from various newspapers attended. Wu Huanzhang first reported on General Ma Zhanshan's retreat into Russia and the date of his return to China, followed by Jiang Songnian's report on the Heilongjiang Army's arduous battles and their detour to Jehol. The meeting adjourned at about 5 PM. The reports of Wu and Jiang are recorded separately below:

Wu Huanzhang's Report 129

I am very honored and fortunate that you, comrades of the press, have graced us with your guidance today. I will briefly report to you on Chairman Ma Zhanshan's journey into Russia, the date of his return to China, and the arrival of the Heilongjiang Army on the border of Jehol.

Journey into Russia and Date of Return 130

The day before yesterday, I received a telegram from Wan Fulin of the Beiping Branch of the Military Commission, relaying Chairman Ma Zhanshan's telegram stating that after issuing the general attack order in October of last year, he besieged the enemy for more than a month in Laha Station, Taian Town, Keshan, and other places. However, due to exhaustion of ammunition and supplies and the arrival of enemy reinforcements, as well as the assistance of Mongolian bandits, our army suffered heavy losses. In order to preserve strength, he ordered the troops on the Qikehu-Hai lines to march west, hoping to establish contact with the Su (Bingwen) army. When they reached Yalu County, they were attacked by the Japanese army attacking Su. He had no choice but to order Bu Binshan, Deng Wen, Tan Zixin, Li Zhongyi, and others to lead their troops west, taking the Solun Mountain in Mongolia towards Jehol, in order to obtain supplies. Chairman Ma personally took the European route, intending to report the atrocities of the violent Japan to the League of Nations. Recently, I received confirmation that the central government has remitted the funds needed by Chairman Ma and Commander Su. Both Ma and Su were extremely indignant at the depth of the enemy's invasion in North China and have submitted a written report to the League of Nations. The trip to Geneva has been canceled, and they are planning to return to China. Chairman Ma, because his troops have arrived on the border of Jehol, will first return to China by a roundabout route to lead his troops and continue to resist Japan.

Situation of the Heilongjiang Army Arriving on the Border of Jehol 131

The various anti-Japanese armies of Heilongjiang Province, led by Commander Deng, Deputy Commander Tan, and Commander Shao, numbered about 15,000 when they arrived on the border of Jehol. Those led by Commander Li Zhongyi numbered about 27,000. In total, the troops that arrived numbered about 40,000. Under the supervision of Chairman Ma, these troops first raised the banner of anti-Japanese resistance, fought bloody battles, and struggled for years. Due to exhaustion of ammunition and clothing, they detoured to Jehol, suffering from hunger and cold, and enduring great hardship. Yesterday, Commander Deng sent a telegram to Mr. Li Mingxin stating that they had no way to raise funds for Ma's team's expenses or to send telegrams. The difficulty of their situation can be seen. These troops have a considerable history of anti-Japanese warfare and have sacrificed a lot of courage. Now that they have come to Jehol due to unavoidable circumstances, we must provide them with adequate supplies as soon as possible so that they can return to Heilongjiang and continue to resist Japan. There are still more than 40,000 troops lurking in various places in Heilongjiang. They will surely follow suit if they see that those who have gone to Jehol have no return date. If so, then Japan will be able to clear all of our border volunteer armies in Heilongjiang Province without spending a single soldier or arrow. This will have a great impact on our country's entire plan to recover lost territory. Moreover, violent Japan's invasion of North China is urgent, and Jehol's safety is precarious. In order to draw firewood from under the cauldron and slow down the enemy's advance, these incoming troops should be actively supplied. In order to allow these troops to join the fighting in Jehol, they should also be actively supplied. In short, with the loss of the Northeast and the instability of North China, the survival of the Chinese nation depends entirely on the result of a desperate fight. Although the Heilongjiang army has failed to achieve its goal of defending the territory, its years of arduous fighting are enough to demonstrate the spirit of our nation. Therefore, supplying these troops will be more effective than regrouping newly formed troops.

Thanking the Press 132

Since Heilongjiang Province first raised the banner of anti-Japanese resistance, the comrades in the Shanghai press have promoted it in many ways, giving Heilongjiang unlimited assistance. Chairman Ma and all the officers and soldiers are extremely grateful. However, the country is in trouble, and we still rely on you, gentlemen, to vigorously promote it so that we can get adequate supplies and complete our unfinished work. It would be fortunate.

Jiang Songnian's Report 133

Mr. Wu Huanzhang has already reported in detail on the purpose of inviting you today. I accompanied Chairman Ma in the war against Japan for half a year, so I know the actual situation of the war in more detail. Therefore, I will report on it. After the violent Japan expanded the incident in the Northeast, the three provinces were lost, and the people of the three provinces lost their support. Chairman Ma took the lead in raising the banner of righteousness to fulfill his duty. At that time, the army carried radios to communicate with various places and report on the war situation at any time. The comrades in the press revealed and promoted it in detail, so that the officers and soldiers fighting hard outside the customs received a lot of spiritual comfort and material assistance, which is very admirable. Later, because the motor was heavy and the rain caused water to accumulate, making it very difficult to transport across the rivers, the machine industry was placed in the mountains. Afterwards, news from the front was cut off, causing the people of the country to be ignorant and leading to rumors of Chairman Ma's hatred. Now, I will report on the situation after the information was cut off as follows:

Three provinces have already fallen, and alarming news has come from Yu and Rehe. Xuezhong has a responsibility to defend the territory and shares the same animosity towards the enemy. I vow to strictly discipline my troops to defend our borders. I am grateful for your clear instruction and express my sincere sentiments. Yu Xuezhong Qin Seal.

Moreover, one party sent Yu south to report everything. When Chairman Ma was about to leave, he said to Yu, "I have two paths ahead: to die resisting Japan or to live resisting Japan." Although Chairman Ma is currently abroad, he will soon return to the country to raise the banner of righteousness again and vow to resist Japan to the death. I am very grateful for your previous efforts in promoting the cause of the anti-Japanese army. I hope you will continue to assist as much as possible. The survival of the Chinese nation rests on this one effort.

News of Ma's Death from a Certain Source

Chairman Ma encountered three thousand enemy soldiers on his way to meet Generals Ding and Li. After a day of fierce fighting, he finally broke through. During this battle, one of Chairman Ma's guards died. This guard wore a Wenhu Medal, which he had received from the chief guard of General Su Bingwen. Initially, when Generals Su and Ma met, General Su's chief guard gave a Wenhu Medal to Chairman Ma's chief guard. After playing with it for a long time, Chairman Ma's chief guard gave it to a guard. This guard then wore the Wenhu Medal on his body and died with it. However, the source of this Wenhu Medal is unknown. Later, the enemy inspected the corpses and suddenly found a body wearing a Wenhu Medal. They were overjoyed, believing that anyone wearing a Wenhu Medal must be a lieutenant general or higher, and the body's height was similar to Chairman Ma's. They mistakenly believed that Chairman Ma was dead. The enemy forces in Heilongjiang Province celebrated for three days and reported it to the Japanese Emperor. However, it has now been proven that Chairman Ma is still alive. Nevertheless, Japanese and puppet newspapers still refer to Chairman Ma as "Second Ma Zhanshan" and "Puppet Ma Zhanshan," etc., because the news has already been reported to the Japanese Emperor.

Telegrams from Wang Delin and Others

Cut off the enemy's advance on all routes from Jilin to Dunhua and Jihui.

Even with one bullet and one man, we will fight to the end.

We still hope for government troops and assistance from compatriots nationwide.

General Wang Delin, Commander-in-Chief of the Jilin National Salvation Army, and all 43 generals including Kong Xianrong, sent a telegram to the nation on the 12th, vowing to fight to the end, hoping for government troops and urgent assistance from compatriots. Every word is tearful and extremely painful. The original telegram was released yesterday by the Northeast Anti-Japanese Army Joint Liaison Office in Shanghai, as follows: To the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, National Government, Chairman Chiang, Beiping Chairman Zhang, all ministries and departments, all provincial and municipal party headquarters, all provincial and municipal governments, all charitable organizations, all military units, all newspapers, and all envoys to China. Since the September 18th Incident, the brutal Japanese have invaded and occupied our land, slaughtered our people, seized political power, and established a puppet state, resorting to all kinds of atrocities. Subsequently, they bombed Shanghai and Tianjin, and their iron hooves have swept across the Northeast. Fortunately, friendly forces have risen up like a storm, vowing to turn the tide, and it has been more than a year. The enemy has not yet fulfilled their beastly desires. Our army has fought hundreds of battles, desperately holding on to a corner, with few bullets and little clothing, enduring ice and snow. This is our duty, and we dare not claim merit. However, from the beginning of his campaign, Delin took it as his responsibility to cut off the enemy's railways from Jilin to Dunhua and Jihui, destroying those already completed and preventing those not yet completed from being built. This is a crucial strategy to prevent the enemy from deploying troops and transporting weapons. To this day, we continue to destroy and rebuild, and any conspiracies and schemes are hindered by transportation obstacles. The impact of this is known to the world. However, because of this restriction and harassment, the enemy is determined to annihilate our army, and they think of this day and night. Delin's ambition is to save the country, and he has no concerns. As long as there is a breath left, this plan will never be relaxed. However, when will the broken land be recovered? Hoping for fair mediation from the League of Nations is like looking at plums to quench thirst, and waiting for a national mobilization is like drawing cakes to satisfy hunger. It is heartbreaking and deeply worrying. Generals Ma and Su have already painfully led their troops into Russia, and Commanders Ding and Li have been forced to gradually retreat north. All of them are well-trained troops with strategic experience and numbers that are superior to our army, yet they have been forced to retreat temporarily due to a lack of ammunition, resulting in unnecessary sacrifices. The facts are there, and even in defeat, they are glorious. We have lost contact, and the oppressive situation of the brutal Japanese is becoming increasingly tight. In recent days, there have been fierce battles in Ning'an, Muling, Mudanjiang, Suifenhe, and along the Jilin-Dunhua railway. Fortunately, our soldiers are fighting bravely, and although the enemy is attacking from above and below with aircraft and heavy artillery, we are relying on the terrain to strike at their weaknesses, and we have not been defeated. Even though there is no medical care for the wounded and dead, the unity and solidarity of our spirit is being forged in day and night battles. Delin has dedicated himself to the Party and the country and is determined to die. He deeply understands that the lack of supplies and ammunition is the most significant suffering. Therefore, he sent Liang Juntang to Guannei as his plenipotentiary representative to appeal to the central authorities, charitable organizations, and overseas Chinese for assistance. To this day, although we have received patriotic support from all sides and have been working hard to provide relief, the funds received are still a drop in the bucket and cannot solve the problem. Delin is currently in a state of isolation and helplessness. I dare to solemnly declare again that even if we fight to the last bullet and the last man, we will fight to the death with the Japanese invaders. We know that under an overturned nest, there can be no intact eggs. However, a common man cannot be deprived of his ambition. We are unwilling to surrender to the enemy and live a life of shame, nor do we want to enter Russia and take a detour.

Japanese Trade with China Last Year

Except for North China, it has decreased overall.

The Shanghai Japanese Commercial Counselor's Office received a telegram from Tokyo on January 18 stating that the total value of Japan's domestic and overseas trade in 1932 was 2,980,000,000 yen, of which exports accounted for only 1,457,000,000 yen, resulting in a surplus of 66,000,000 yen. Compared to the previous year, the total value of foreign trade increased by 20%, exports increased by 24%, imports increased by 15%, and the surplus decreased by 50%. The increase in imports was mainly due to cotton, wool, iron, machinery, kerosene, wheat, and other raw materials. Importers anticipated that prices would rise due to increased import taxes and inflation, leading to competitive imports. As for export trade, it was very active in all regions except China and the United States. Cotton cloth, silk, socks, porcelain, etc., were very popular in India, the Dutch East Indies, Vietnam, Australia, New Zealand, Egypt, Aden, Britain, France, Belgium, Italy, and South America due to the low exchange rate of the Japanese currency. There was also a great demand for cotton cloth, flour, machinery, sugar, and other groceries in Manchuria. As for trade with China, the total value of exports for the year was 147,000,000 yen, resulting in a surplus of 69,000,000 yen. Compared to the previous year, exports to North China increased by 46% (almost half), while exports to Central China decreased by 39%, exports to South China decreased by 92%, and exports to Hong Kong decreased by 59%. Conversely, imports from China to Japan decreased by 18% from North China, 32% from Central China, 28% from South China, and 95% from Hong Kong. In Manchuria, the total value of exports for the year was 146,000,000 yen, resulting in a surplus of 18,000,000 yen, with exports increasing by 89% and imports decreasing by 2% compared to the previous year.

The Rumor of the Turpan Rebellion is Inaccurate

Turkish Press Telegram to Shanghai Muslims

The Rumor Was Fabricated by an Istanbul Correspondent

According to Xin Sheng She, the rumor of a rebellion in Turpan, Xinjiang, and the intention to establish a buffer state between China and Russia similar to the puppet state of Manchuria, which was transmitted by a Russian telegram from Istanbul, Turkey, has already been denied by influential Muslims in Shanghai. It is further heard that the Muslim community has now received a reply telegram from the Istanbul press, stating that the Turkish society does not pay attention to this news. Only a few days ago, a Turkish newspaper published a similar piece of news, which was said to have been sent by an Oriental correspondent stationed in Turkey. Therefore, the previous unfounded rumor has been clarified, and the intention of the rumor-monger is known.

Regardless of whether rear support is timely, we will resist for a long time in the White Mountains and Black Waters with our 70,000 loyal and brave soldiers. We hope to cooperate with the national army in a joint expedition to capture the Yellow Dragon. Our strategy may change, but our will will never waver. Finally, we still hope that the government will send troops for assistance, and that our compatriots will pay special attention and strive to find solutions. We eagerly await your help. We express our plea with tears in our eyes, hoping for your understanding. General Wang Delin, Commander-in-Chief of the National Salvation Army, along with Vice Commander and Brigade Commander, Central Route Commander Kong Rong, Left Route Commander and Brigade Commander Wang Yuzhen, Right Route Commander and Brigade Commander Wu Yichen, Brigade Commanders Chen Yuqing, Zhang Peng, Yang Xisan, Li Zhaodong, Chen Wanlin, Cheng Haifeng, Pacification Commander Yu Xuanrui,督战Commander Zhang Yuting, Regiment Commanders Zheng Xing, Li Yanlu, Jiang Bingshan, Ma Haishan, Zhang Xiangyun, Meng Xianshu, Chen Deshun, Sun Baokun, Liu Jingchen, Wen Mingshan, Gong Yinqing, Zu Yaozhong, Wang Kaichen, Yao Shuyun, Liu Shikai, Zou Jingfu, Sun Hongen, Zhou Donghua, Du Liansheng, Mu Xingyun, Chai Shirong, Wu Hanchen, Yu Fenggang, Shi Xiaodong, Yao Zhenshan, Shan Bingjun, Wei Zhenshan, Liang Dengcheng, Sun Dengshan, Yang Deshan, Ai Lantai, Yin Yongnian, etc., respectfully kowtow.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Major Layoffs

More Than One Hundred Laid-Off Workers at Five Wharves Petition Yesterday

Since Liu Hongsheng took over as general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, he has been trying to reorganize the company. One hundred and six redundant employees in the head office have been laid off. A notice was issued the day before yesterday to lay off 117 employees at the five wharves. The union held a general meeting yesterday, and the entire body petitioned the board of directors in the afternoon. The details are as follows:

Continued Layoffs

The board of directors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company announced the day before yesterday that 117 employees at the five wharves would be laid off. The original letter is as follows: "To whom it may concern: By order of the general manager, the company's finances are strained. The employees in question should be immediately suspended from their duties, etc. This is to inform you to check and hand over all matters in your charge, and then collect your severance pay." The severance pay method is calculated based on the number of years of service: one month's salary for those with less than one year of service, and two months' salary for those with one year or more of service. All those who are not laid off will also be notified by letter.

Union Meeting

After receiving reports from the heads of the various groups at the five wharves, the union immediately registered the laid-off employees. There were 12 laid-off employees from the North Wharf, 36 from the China Wharf, 13 from the Central Wharf, 17 from the South Wharf, and 23 from the New Wharf, totaling 101 people. The remaining 16 people were not registered. An emergency meeting was immediately convened at 10:00 AM yesterday. It was resolved that the layoffs were unfair. It was resolved to 1) nominate Fu Ziyang (China Wharf), Chen Shifu (South Wharf), Chen Mei (New Wharf), Li Angqing (North Wharf), Shan Xishou (South Wharf), and Jiang Yinkui (North Wharf) to petition the board of directors and demand the recall of the order; 2) issue a declaration requesting assistance from the party and government organs.

Collective Petition

At 3:00 PM yesterday, the union of the five wharves sent Fu Ziyang, Chen Shifu, Chen Mei, and others to lead all the laid-off employees to the board of directors of the head office to petition and demand the recall of the order. The board of directors was holding its tenth regular meeting. After the meeting adjourned, Du Yuesheng, a standing director, met with them. The union representatives first stated the unfairness of the layoffs. Du Yuesheng then ordered the union to submit detailed reasons and malpractices of each wharf to the board of directors, which would then review and remedy the situation. The entire body of employees was satisfied and dispersed.

General Manager's Statement

A reporter from Xin Sheng She met with General Manager Liu Hongsheng last night. According to him, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has too much debt. The total annual turnover is only more than 5 million yuan, but the salaries of employees are very high and there are many redundant employees. The financial situation is strained, and it is necessary to lay off employees at the five wharves. The results of the inspections by the heads of the various departments and the review by the board of directors were approved. In addition to paying severance pay to the laid-off employees in accordance with the regulations, the wages for December and double pay will be paid in full.

Dismissal of Third Mates

The second layoff of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was carried out yesterday. In addition to one month's salary, each laid-off person will receive one month's severance pay. Yesterday, the ship captains were notified to go to the company to collect the money on their behalf, and the laid-off employees were ordered to leave the ships immediately.

Page 10

The company order is recorded as follows: To the order of compliance, in the case of the first class of driving students from the former Navigation School, who graduated in June last year, all of them were used as alternate third mates, but the company's ships are too small, and there is no need for third mates. After selecting the best of the students to act as alternate second mates for four of them, the rest were still assigned to the ships for internship. This has been extended for a long time, which has not only hindered the students' future, but also prevented other nautical students from having equal opportunities to practice. It is not appropriate for both of them. The Ministry of Communications has repeatedly ordered the students of the Wusong Merchant Marine School's driving class to be assigned to various ships for practice, and the board of directors has considered the sticky fruit and agreed that the equal practice and macro-creation should be the proper way. The alternate third mates should be dismissed, and the allowance should be stopped by the end of this month. In the future, if there is a vacancy in the company's ships, the best of them should still be given priority. The number of people to be dismissed is attached to the back, and the captains of each ship are instructed to comply. Sincerely, this order. It is planned to dismiss ten alternate third mates: Chen Shuding (Jianghua), Teng Jiufan (Jiangxin), Zhou Hongyin (Jiangxin), You Junyuan (Jiangda), Xiao Jinan (Gongping), Lu Yuexue (Gongping), Tu Fang (Guangli), He Tong (Guonan), Xu Guangshi (Yushun), Gao Fakang (Jiahe). French Concession Taxpayers Association Opposes Water and Electricity Price Increases

Westerners Request Chinese Directors to Strictly Reject

The French Concession Taxpayers Association sent a letter to the Chinese directors of the French Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "To whom it may concern, according to letters from citizens Zhang Zhongfang, Lu Guisheng, etc., it has recently been heard that the French-owned water and electricity company in the French Concession is considering increasing the price of water and electricity, and a proposal may soon be submitted for the French Municipal Council to review and approve. Since the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, the market has been depressed, and the people's livelihood has been declining. The situation of recession is becoming increasingly obvious. Even taking measures to provide relief is not enough. Now the company, as a local public utility operated exclusively, disregards the people's livelihood and suddenly wants to increase the burden on residents. The citizens vow not to recognize this. Please forward this to the Chinese directors attending the French Municipal Council and do not accept the proposal for the benefit of the people. The water and electricity are public utilities that are closely related to the daily needs of the people. They cannot be regarded as a source of profit, only to seek business gains. Judging from the original water and electricity prices set by the French company, they are already expensive compared to the Public Concession. At that time, it may have been the initial stage, and there were few users. For the sake of maintaining the blood capital, it was not too harsh. Now, the concession is prosperous, and the residents are close together. The company's business is developed, and the profits are already considerable. Yet, it is still not satisfied and wants to increase the price, which violates the purpose of public utilities, and the local residents cannot recognize this. In accordance with the foregoing, this is to inform you that if the French water and electricity company requests the Municipal Council to increase the price, please strictly reject it and do not allow it to pass in order to benefit the people's livelihood and maintain public welfare. It is for the public good."

Pirates Hijack the Dahua Steamer Outside Wusongkou

The Pirates Infiltrated from Shanghai

Robbery of New Banknotes from Farmers and Workers

Losses Exceeded 30,000 Gold

Fortunately, Passengers Were Safe

In recent times, merchant ships along the coast of Zhejiang have been repeatedly hijacked by pirates. First, there was the Yongchuan, then the Xinningtai, and now the Shanghai-Zhoushan steamer Dahua has suffered a significant loss. The details of the investigation obtained by the reporter of this newspaper are recorded below:

Cause of the Hijacking

It is recalled that two months ago, the Customs received a confidential report stating that dozens of pirates from Dapeng Bay had set off for the coast of Zhejiang, intending to loot merchant ships. The confidential order required all shipping companies to pay attention. This matter was recorded in this newspaper, but after a long time, the shipping industry no longer remembers. However, these pirates have been hiding in Shanghai, specializing in investigating ships carrying large sums of money in order to carry out robberies. This time, the Agricultural and Industrial Bank issued new banknotes, and a batch of them was transported to Zhoushan on the Dahua. The bandits discovered this, so they gathered people to board the ship and carry out the robbery.

Disguised as Passengers

The Dahua Steamer of the Ping An Company, which runs between Shanghai and Zhoushan, is assigned to the Lian'an Shipping Bureau. It departed from Nanshi, Shanghai, at 3:00 PM on the 17th of this month. There were more than 400 passengers on board, and the 15 pirates boarded the ship in Shanghai as passengers. Weapons such as pistols were carried in luggage and other items. When the ship set sail, the 15 pirates were scattered in various cabins, waiting for the ship to reach Wusongkou to carry out the robbery.

Details of the Robbery

At 7:40 PM on the 17th, the ship sailed to the area between the No. 1 river cylinder and the No. 2 river brief outside Wusongkou. At that time, the passengers had finished their dinner and were preparing to sleep. Among the 15 pirates, four of them sneaked out of the cabin, fired a shot into the sky, and rushed into the captain's room. The captain, Ge, and all the crew members were guarded and imprisoned in one room. Then, they began to loot, first robbing the accounting room, taking more than 500 yuan in silver dollars and more than 100 yuan in small coins that had been sold. Four female students from a school in Hangzhou were robbed of more than 2,000 yuan in silver dollars. The abbot of Baoben Temple in Mount Putuo, Ying Zhao, was robbed of 350 yuan in paper money and silver dollars. Because he refused to be searched, he was beaten and eventually robbed.

Robbery of New Banknotes

The bandits' purpose was the large sum of new banknotes from the Agricultural and Industrial Bank, totaling 20,000 yuan. They were shipped from Shanghai to the Zhoushan branch and stored in the silver cabin. The bandits forced the accountant to open the silver cabin and took all 20,000 yuan in new banknotes. At that time, the sky was slightly bright. Some of the pirates who were familiar with driving skills drove the Dahua to the Huanglong Jiao Reef outside Sanjiashui, Wusong, preparing to escape.

Looting and Fleeing Far Away

On the 18th, the Dahua arrived at Huanglong Jiao Reef and immediately stopped. The stolen silver and other items were packed into several bags, and the captain, Ge, and the passenger Hong were forced to board two small boats to transport the bandits to the small island of Jiao Reef. Fearing that something might happen, they also ordered the captain to send the bandits to the island. The captain and others had no choice but to obey. When the bandits left, they fired several shots (pistols) on the edge of the small island. The bandits had a small boat waiting for them, so they were able to escape safely.

Telegram to Shanghai

The Dahua Steamer is only 600 tons and has no radio equipment, so it was unable to report the robbery. After the bandits fled, the captain returned to the ship, released the crew members, and rushed to Dinghai. It was afternoon when they arrived in Dinghai, and the captain sent a telegram to Shanghai, reporting to the Lian'an Shipping Bureau that the Dahua had been robbed at Songkou, that the passengers were safe, and that they had arrived in Dinghai. The telegram arrived in Shanghai on the night of the 18th. It is estimated that the ship will arrive at Haimen yesterday. Yesterday, a reporter went to the Lian'an Shipping Bureau. According to Director Dong, the Shanghai Bureau had sent a telegram to Haimen, ordering the Dahua to return to Shanghai as soon as possible to investigate the truth. In total, the public and private losses from this robbery are estimated to be more than 10,000 yuan. Fortunately, no passengers or crew members were injured.

Former Contractor of Tea and Snacks on Shanghai-Hangzhou Passenger Trains Causes Disturbance at the North Station Yesterday

According to the Central News Agency, at 9:00 AM yesterday, a man claiming to be Sun Wenpin, the manager of the tea and snack contract for the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo passenger trains, and dozens of workers and their families broke into the office of the director of the train affairs department, demanding the cancellation of the bidding for the tea and snack contract for the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway. They claimed that Sun Wenpin's contract was not due to expire until the end of July, and that 3,000 yuan had been deposited as proof. Zheng Baozhao, the director of the train affairs department, and Yuan Boyang, the deputy director of the general affairs department, repeatedly tried to persuade them, but they refused to leave and became even more aggressive, occupying the office and threatening them. The order was quite chaotic for a while. The stalemate lasted until 3:00 PM without any results. Finally, the police station sent police officers to disperse them and arrested two masterminds on the spot. Afterwards, inquiries were made to the responsible parties of the railway bureau. According to them, Sun Wenpin's contract for the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway had expired in July last year. The former director, Chen Xinghan, had approved a renewal of the contract and ordered Sun Wenpin to deposit 1,000 yuan as a guarantee, pending approval. However, this matter has not yet been determined, and Sun Wenpin published a newspaper advertisement claiming to be the contractor, which was close to fraud. The Public Security Bureau questioned the railway bureau, which resulted in the contract not being approved and signed. The bureau is now publicly bidding to avoid private malfeasance. There are no restrictions on the qualifications of bidders or restrictions on Sun Wenpin from bidding. The bureau has not signed the renewal contract, so it does not bear any legal responsibility. The so-called tea and snack workers on the two railways are not railway workers, and the Central Government has explained this in the past. They are just contractors. Sun Wenpin claimed to be a tea and snack worker and attempted to cause trouble at the North Station. The military and police organs in Shanghai have taken strict measures to ensure safety.

Chinese Medical Association
