It is hoped that rescue and protection personnel from all ports will hear the news and register with the association's general and branch associations to jointly relieve the national crisis.

Wusong Steamer Relief Association

Petitioned Party and Government Organs Yesterday

Tong Hu Mingchen, Arrested in Hankou, Could Arrive

Mutual Aid Society Demands Bail from Jardine Matheson Taipan

According to Xin Sheng She, since the Jardine Matheson Taipan of the British company Jardine Matheson became embroiled in the Wusong dispute, two people, the deputy comprador Tong Chunhua and the accountant Hu Henian, have been arrested by the Hankou Haichang and sent to Shanghai by the Changxing Steamer of the Sanbei Company under police escort for investigation. The Relief Association sent personnel yesterday to petition the authorities to strictly investigate the case. The details are as follows:

De Facto Detention

It was originally scheduled that the Wusong Steamer would arrive in Shanghai yesterday. According to reliable sources, because the steamer forcibly expelled the sailors in the middle cabin, it aroused the anger of the sailors in Hankou, which resulted in the steamer's cargo not being unloaded, and there is a de facto detention.

Petition for Strict Investigation

At 10:00 AM yesterday, the Wusong Steamer Tragedy Relief Association sent representatives Lu Shuangxi, Jiang Youming, and Shi Dianchen, representatives of the sailors in the middle cabin of the Wusong Steamer, and more than 20 other people to the Municipal Government, the Social Bureau, and the Special Municipal Party Headquarters of the Sailors' Union to petition for a strict investigation of Tong Chunhua and Hu Henian. At the same time, they demanded a swift mediation so that work

Delegation desired to meet Ma 135

When the League of Nations investigation delegation arrived in Shanghai, Chairman Ma sent Yu to Shanghai to observe the attitude of the Chinese people and secretly followed them from Beijing to Peiping to Shenyang. At that time, I planned to visit and report the actual situation, but ultimately gave up due to the strict Japanese military alert and the sincere advice of friends. Later, the investigation delegation went to Harbin. At that time, I disregarded everything and ventured to visit. Fortunately, with the help of a certain gentleman, arrangements were made in advance, and we finally met on May 15th at a certain place. We talked for two hours, and I reported all the facts in detail. At that time, the members of the investigation delegation were very willing to meet Chairman Ma, so I discussed the date and location with them. Although Chairman Ma had not yet entered Hailun, in order to facilitate this, I deliberately told them that he had arrived, and told them that in addition to the danger of Japanese planes on the journey, he was willing to take full responsibility, and could even order all the soldiers to line up along the railway line for alert. At that time, the members of the investigation delegation were all delighted, and then bid farewell, led by a certain Westerner, crossed from the basement into the neighboring house and went out, then secretly crossed the Songhua River and returned north. At that time, rumors of Japanese military attacks had spread in Hailun, and the people, supporting the old and carrying the young, were on the way in an endless stream. The next day, I went further south to Hailun to meet the members of the investigation delegation again, but their attitude had changed from yesterday, and they were unwilling to go north. I tried to persuade them to no avail. This was probably due to the bewitchment of the Japanese. Knowing that it was impossible to force them, I returned. On the evening of the 19th, the investigation delegation also left Harbin and returned south. Later, Chairman Ma met with two American reporters from the New York Times on the way to retreat from Hailun. They secretly took a train north, and then carried their luggage and trudged forward. They first encountered bandits, and when they told them where they were going, they were not harmed, but instead were led forward. When they reached the outpost of the Black Army, they left. Only then did the sentinel soldiers realize that they were bandits, but they did not pursue them. When the two reporters went to meet Chairman Ma, I was also present, writing down the actual situation, all in a huge volume. When they said goodbye, Chairman Ma also sent a car and dispatched soldiers to escort them. The people along the way warmly welcomed them, and there were even those who emptied the entire city to welcome them. The sincerity of the people can be imagined. When they returned to Harbin, the Japanese side learned of it, and they were arrested. Finally, all the documents were confiscated, but they were spared from disaster. One of them has now returned to his country, and the other is still staying in China. When I came here, I also met them and talked about everything, it is said.

The Course of Retreating from Hailun 136

Chairman Ma entered Hailun in May to command the anti-Japanese military affairs of Heilongjiang Province. At that time, the enemy army knew that Chairman Ma had arrived in Hailun, so they sent many planes to hover over the sky of Hailun every day and carry out bombing. I arrived in Hailun in late May. On May 30th, I was talking with Chairman Ma and others in a room when eight enemy planes soared in the air, their sights all focused on the room where Chairman Ma lived. Bombs fell like rain. Fortunately, the wind was very strong that day, and none of them hit. We had no choice but to accompany Chairman Ma out of the house and walk to avoid danger. However, the enemy planes tracked us left and right, firing machine guns. Chairman Ma and I took cover under the eaves, and bullets hit the roof tiles, and mud and ash fell, all brushing past the brims of our hats. For the sake of Chairman Ma's safety, we strongly advised Chairman Ma to leave Hailun temporarily and go to the countryside to avoid enemy planes. Chairman Ma firmly refused, willing to perish with Hailun. By that evening, the houses of the people in Hailun City were destroyed by enemy bombs everywhere, and the people were dying in piles, a tragic sight. For the sake of the safety of the surviving victims in the city, Chairman Ma finally sadly left Hailun that evening and left first.

Enduring Hunger and Cold in Bitter Fighting 137

After Chairman Ma met with the two reporters after retreating from Hailun, he led more than 1,000 troops to meet with Ding Chao and Li Du. The Japanese army learned of this and sent three armored ships to pursue them by water, and also sent more than 2,000 soldiers to surround them by land. Because they were outnumbered, they entered the deep mountains. The land there was mostly fine mud, which was so deep that it could submerge their shins, making it difficult to walk. Soldiers and horses collapsed from exhaustion. They only traveled more than 40 li a day. The food they carried was only two sheng of millet per person, and the mountain road was long and far, 400 li, with no trace of human habitation around. The food was about to run out, so they had no choice but to leave the mountains. When they encountered the Japanese army, they dispersed and fought back in the pond fields. The enemy's encirclement and attack were unsuccessful, so they retreated into the deep mountains again. They had nothing to eat for two days after the food ran out, so they had no choice but to slaughter old and weak horses, roast them, and eat them to satisfy their hunger. In the mountains, old trees provided shade, and dead leaves fell, as deep as a foot. Only dirty water accumulated. They slept on it at night, and their clothes were completely wet. Moreover, it rained a lot in the mountains. Their suffering was truly beyond words. At this time, Chairman Ma was not in good health. Every night, he would lay wooden branches on the ground and sleep in the open air, still happy and not feeling any pain. His spirit of vowing to die for the country can be imagined. As they advanced further, they saw a village house inhabited by those who privately planted opium. They stored a lot of grain. The soldiers all looked hungry and planned to buy food at a fair price. One of them, who used to be a battalion commander, recognized Chairman Ma and donated all the 100 dan of white flour and 200 shi of rice he had stored, leaving only a small amount for food. Chairman Ma firmly declined, but to no avail. Each soldier received two sheng of rice. Advancing further, they saw a train station after a month's journey. Knowing that they were near Qiqihar, the soldiers were wildly happy, urging their horses to gallop, eager to see houses, people, and animals first. After Chairman Ma met with Ding and Li, he handed over the troops to the two army commanders of the Tan Department and led them into Rehe. He himself went to see Cai Tingkai, He Zhuguo, etc. in secret.

Telegram to Shanghai from All Circles Unite to Resist Insults 138

Implement the Original Intention of the Shanghai Battle and Fight to the End

The Army and People are United, and Morale is Available

The National Salvation Joint Conference of various groups in this city, because the situation in Rehe and Yu was tense, in addition to sending representatives such as Sheng Minxiu to Shanhaiguan and other places to comfort the anti-Japanese soldiers, also telegraphed various military leaders to quickly provide assistance. Watchman Angered, Wife Ran Away, Committed Suicide by Hanging 140

Li Qingrong, a native of Shandong, 41 years old, lived at No. 13, Yuan Yi Fang, Yangshupu Road, and was a watchman. In May, his wife, Ms. Someone, suddenly ran away. Although Li sent people to search in all directions, he has not been found to this day. Because of this, Li was often annoyed in his heart, so he suddenly had the idea of ending his life the day before yesterday, and committed suicide by hanging himself in his bedroom alone. After Lin Changgen noticed, he immediately reported to the Yangshupu Police Station and ordered detectives to investigate. After the investigation, they sent him to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but he had already died of suffocation. Then, the corpse was carried to the corpse examination office on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, they reported to the First Special District Local Court and appointed Prosecutor Guo Wei to come to the office to examine the corpse. After taking the case, he questioned Lin Changgen about the situation at the time. Mr. Guo then announced that the deceased, Li Qingrong, had committed suicide by hanging himself before his death. The corpse was handed over to his brother, Li Qingquan, to lead back to the coffin.

Carpenter Sentenced to Life Imprisonment for Raping a Young Girl 141

Zhang Liqiang, a native of Fenghua, Ningbo, 32 years old, a carpenter, lived at No. 14, Pingliang Road. At about 7 pm on the 4th of this month, he stayed in Dahua Department Store at No. 1432, Wuzhou Road to settle the debt. It happened that A Su, the seven-year-old daughter of a neighboring Cantonese woman, Zheng Wang, went to the company to play. Zhang was inherently lustful, had been a regular at brothels, and suffered from leukorrhea. Seeing that A Su was petite and exquisite, he suddenly had beastly desires. He lured her into the bedroom behind the store, covered her with a quilt, first teased her, then took off her pants, and raped her. Later, her mother found that her lower body was red and swollen and had white discharge when bathing A Su. After interrogating her about what happened, she reported to the Jiaxing Road Police Station and sent Chinese detective Peng Yushan to arrest Zhang and send A Su to Shanghai Convalescent Hospital on Lao Ba Zi Road. The doctor found that her hymen was ruptured and she was infected with leukorrhea, which would be difficult to cure for life. Zhang was sent to the First Special District Court. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that in recent years, cases of luring and raping young girls have occurred one after another in society, and morality and conscience have been lost. Zhang was suffering from leukorrhea and raped A Su, causing the girl's future happiness to be completely sacrificed. He requested that the defendant be given a severe sentence to warn others against following his example. After a detailed interrogation and clear confession in court, it was announced that the arguments had ended and the verdict would be announced. As reported in this newspaper, yesterday, Judge Zhao Linyu and Chief Prosecutor Wang Zuze came to the Third Criminal Court to announce the verdict that Zhang Liqiang was sentenced to life imprisonment for raping a girl under the age of sixteen and causing serious injury, and deprived of his civil rights for life.

Second Council Meeting of the Aviation Association 142

| Passed Various Regulations and Set Up a Clubhouse |

The China Aviation Association held its second council meeting at 3 pm yesterday in the auditorium of the Municipal Government on Fenglin Bridge. Ten council members, including Wang Xiaolai, Shi Liangcai, Hu Yunzhuang, Dai Kuisheng, Lin Wojiang, Lin Kanghou, Wang Zhiyuan, Chen Guangfu, Liu Peiquan, and Huang Bingxian, attended. Wang Xiaolai chaired the meeting, and Li Dachao took the minutes. The meeting proceeded as scheduled. The meeting's proceedings were as follows: (A)

Reported Items: 1) No. 99, Avenue Joffre has been designated as the association's address. 2) The operating expenses of 10,000 yuan have been temporarily borrowed from Mayor Wu for use. 3) The previous resolutions were read. (B) Resolutions

Items: 1) The Articles of Association of the China Aviation Association were approved with amendments. 2) The Rules of Procedure for the Council Meeting of the China Aviation Association, the Rules of Procedure for the Standing Committee Meeting, and the Guidelines for Association Affairs were resolved to be reviewed by the three council members Wu Zhiyuan, Liu Peiquan, and Huang Bingheng, and then submitted to the Standing Committee for implementation, and then submitted to the next council meeting for ratification, convened by Council Member Huang. 3) The Propaganda Methods of the China Aviation Association were resolved to be handled by the Standing Committee. 4) The matter of soliciting members was resolved to be handled by Council Member Hu Yunzhuang in conjunction with the Standing Committee. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Postponement of Memorial Service for Battalion Commander An by Muslims 143

After the Fall of Yuguan, the death of Battalion Commander An Dexin in Yuguan was mourned by the whole country. An was a Muslim, so the Muslims in this city originally scheduled to hold a memorial service at the Qinglian Street Mosque in Nine Acres at 9 am yesterday to express their condolences. However, because Muslims from all over the country believed that An's death for the country was a glorious history for Muslims, they sent letters and telegrams to the Shanghai Mosque, requesting a postponement so that Muslims from afar could come to Shanghai to participate in the grand ceremony. Therefore, the mosque has changed the date to 9 am on the 29th of this month, still at the original location.

Temporary Members of the Russian Company of the Public Concession Volunteers to be Employed Long-Term 144

Already Approved by the Board of Directors

During the martial law period in this city last year, the Russian Company of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps temporarily recruited a number of members. Subsequently, in July, the Municipal Council approved the temporary retention of the 73 newly recruited Russian members until the end of the year, when the financial situation would be considered. On the 20th of last month, the Finance Committee discussed the matter and the commander of the Volunteer Corps reported that, according to the previous decision, these extra personnel could be temporarily retained pending the discussion of the budget. The Acting Director of the Finance Department believed that whether to retain them should be decided before considering the Volunteer Corps budget. The commander of the Volunteer Corps continued to state that the current number of Russian Company members, including these 73, was only enough to form the basic needs of three infantry companies in times of emergency. Each of these members costs about 1,000 taels of silver per year, and 73 members would require an additional expense of about 73,000 taels of silver. The committee then discussed the matter and concluded that, even in times of financial difficulty, dismissing these 73 people was not an economical solution. It was decided to retain these members long-term. This case was subsequently submitted to the Board of Directors on January 18 and has been adopted and implemented by the Board of Directors.

Abolition of Tael and Adoption of Yuan 145

Coinage Standard Decided

Lin Kanghou Talks About the Reasons for the Stalled Progress

According to the Central News Agency, the issue of abolishing the tael and adopting the yuan has stalled in effect. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Lin Kanghou at the Bankers' Association yesterday to inquire about the reasons for the stall. According to him, Finance Minister Song Ziwen has repeatedly consulted with the Shanghai banking community on the issue of abolishing the tael and adopting the yuan, and considerable progress has been made. The reason why it has not been realized is that the improper assembly of machinery in the mint is one of the reasons for the stalled progress of the case, and the Japanese invasion of Yuguan is also sufficient to restrain the progress of the case. However, Minister Song hopes to resolve this case in the shortest possible time, so he gathered the Shanghai banking community again at the end of last year to continue the discussion. It is heard that the coinage standard has been decided, etc., it is said.

Reader Advisor

The Way Out for Apprentices 152

丨Letter from Mr. Zhu Shulin丨

Unfortunately, due to poverty, I dropped out of junior high school without graduating! Naturally, the only way out for us young people who drop out halfway is to become shop apprentices. I couldn't escape the control of this environment, so I came to this lifeless old-fashioned shop to be an unfortunate apprentice. However, I have my hopes, and I am determined not to stagnate and not move forward. I am always preparing to work hard. I think: students are the future masters of the country, and their future prospects are very great, but like me, I have no knowledge, where in society is my place to stand? Now that the Examination Yuan has been established, everyone must pass an examination to find a job, and applying for the examination requires certain qualifications, such as graduating from middle school, graduating from university, studying foreign trade, etc. I do not have any of these qualifications. Should I go back to school? That cannot be done, so I cannot take the exam. If I cannot take the exam, how will I find a job in the future? Alas! I am extremely panicked! Please, sir, think of a good way to guide me!

Reply: There are three questions to answer in your letter: The first is the [apprentice] question. Judging from the meaning of the letter, you seem to regard being an apprentice as unfortunate, and this should also be studied separately. If you look at the entire class of apprentices (tens of thousands) and put them in your eyes, and contrast them with those who are well-fed and well-clothed, who own huge sums of money, and who have powerful people driving in high carriages, and discover the unhappiness of the apprentices, this is correct. If you only see those who are rich and powerful and envy them, thinking, [they are men, and I am also a man], why can they be promoted and get rich, but I cannot? Between the square inches, admiration arises, and if it develops from this, and if you are lucky, you will also become a rich and powerful person in the future, then the result will not be the same as them? Once you become the boss, you will treat your apprentices in the same way as your boss treats you now, or perhaps even more severely, then your idea today is wrong. The second is the problem of [students] and [the future masters of the country]. Normally speaking, students are naturally [the future masters of the country]. In fact, the positions that students stand on are also different. From A's point of view, students in A's position are the masters, while students in his position are in the ranks of the oppressed. Similarly, when students in his position are the masters, students in A's position are again oppressed. Therefore, the sentence [students are the future masters of the country], strictly speaking, is really illogical. It would be more reasonable to say that young students of a certain class are the future masters of the country or society. The third is the [examination] problem. In fact, the government's examination is only limited to civil servants, and it does not mean that everyone must pass the examination to eat. Civil servants are some officials, do you envy them? That means your [official heart] has not retreated, otherwise, what are you afraid of? Isn't it good to be an apprentice? If you can wholeheartedly be a top-notch person in the apprentice society, fight for more freedom for the apprentice society, and give the apprentice society more happiness, even if you suffer yourself, that is actually nobler than being a high official or a big boss. Otherwise, you will, by fate, climb to the point of being an official, and be able to make a few official-style articles of [and so on] [pursuant to this], write a few [Mr. Eight-Sided-Sharp] test papers, or be promoted to the position of old boss, with a few pennies, that is only adding a new comrade to the team of bureaucrats and rich people, and adding an enemy to the shop assistants and apprentices. We definitely don't want you to have such thoughts.

Undeliverable Letters 153

㈠ To Mr. Lu Dafeng: Marriage between people with the same surname was not allowed in the past, but according to the current Civil Code, there is no such restriction. It only stipulates: 1. Direct blood relatives and direct in-laws; 2. Collateral blood relatives and collateral in-laws of different generations (but collateral blood relatives beyond the eighth degree and collateral in-laws beyond the fifth degree are not subject to this restriction); 3. Collateral blood relatives of the same generation within the eighth degree (cousins are not subject to this restriction) cannot marry. If the [distant ancestor without mourning garments] mentioned in your letter can be calculated to be outside the above-mentioned kinship, although the same surname can be married without hindrance. Moreover, marriage autonomy is clearly stated in the law, and the other party has reached adulthood (20 years old), so they can freely marry anyone. ㈡ To Mr. Ma Xiangsan: High talent admired, but this newspaper cannot hire you for the time being, please forgive me!

England

Sending Students to Study in China 156

丨Miss Dou is the First丨

To the Education Research Institute of Sun Yat-sen University

Zhuang Yixuanbo, director of the Education Research Institute of National Sun Yat-sen University in Guangzhou, attended the World Education Conference in Europe last summer and reported on the recent situation of new education in China, which was greatly welcomed by people from various countries. When passing through London, he received a letter from the University Federation Committee established in London by the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee to various parts of Britain to give lectures. Dr. Zhuang politely declined due to time constraints. Recently, the committee followed the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Agreement to send students to study in China. Miss Dou (Miss Darroch) was the first to be sent to the institute to study Chinese education issues. Miss Dou grew up in China in her childhood and is proficient in Chinese. After returning to England, she specialized in education at the University of Edinburgh. After graduating, she served as a teacher in primary and secondary schools in that country. Recently, she served as a researcher at the Imperial Education Research Institute in London. She was selected from among many applicants to be sent to China this time and can be called the first person formally sent to China by Britain to study abroad. After arriving in Guangdong, she has discussed research steps in detail with Dr. Zhuang and decided to go north to conduct field investigations and collect data in the near future, and then return to Guangdong in May and June to organize the results and prepare a report. Dr. Zhuang has introduced her to primary and secondary schools in Fujian, Guangdong, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Pingjin, and other countries in Western Europe to visit, and has met with important officials of the Ministry of Education.

Zhou Fohai, Director of the Jiangsu Education Department

Announcement to Student Parents 157

Schools hope for family support

Families should collaborate with schools

Zhou Fohai, Director of the Jiangsu Department of Education, in light of the prevailing poor academic atmosphere, superficial learning, and cries of educational bankruptcy heard across the nation in recent years, believes that to remedy the situation, it is necessary to first rectify academic conduct. This can only be achieved through the combined efforts of both schools and families to achieve complete success. Therefore, regarding the strengths and weaknesses of students' personalities, changes in their thinking, the quality of their habits, and their diligence in studies, if there are aspects the school cannot fully understand, parents should communicate these, providing guidance. Furthermore, regarding the school's discipline and whether students follow the corrections of teachers, and whether students can improve, the family should also assist and urge them to put the corrections into practice. Close collaboration between families and schools is essential for rectification. Two types of forms have been designed. One is a report on the general academic and behavioral status of primary and secondary school students, to be filled out by the school, reporting on the student's academic performance and conduct during the semester to the parents, and including matters for which the school hopes for parental support. The other is a parent report form, to be filled out by the parents before the start of each semester, reporting to the school on the student's condition at home during the holidays, and including matters for which the parents hope for support from the school. Director Zhou also personally wrote a letter to student parents, hoping that all parents would sincerely assist in areas where the school falls short. The letter is several thousand words long and extremely earnest. However, due to the imminent end of the current semester, it could not be implemented. Instructions have been issued to all public and private primary and secondary schools in the province to implement it at the end of the next semester, and to closely observe each item on the form during normal times as a basis for future reporting, and not to do it perfunctorily or superficially. All family communications and parent-teacher conferences should still be held regularly to provide more opportunities for family contact.

Attached: Director Zhou's Letter to Parents of All Jiangsu Students 158

In recent years, academic conduct has declined, learning has become superficial, and cries of educational bankruptcy have been heard across the nation. Informed people are deeply concerned. Based on my observations, I deeply understand that to remedy the situation, it is necessary to first rectify academic conduct. To rectify academic conduct, it is necessary to combine the efforts of both schools and families to achieve complete success. Therefore, I offer my humble thoughts, hoping that you will understand, consider, and adopt them.

In the past, some, clinging to the name of liberalism, vigorously advocated a free academic atmosphere. One person initiated it, and the whole world followed suit. This led to today's bad habits, viewing resistance to authority and violation of discipline as revolutionary spirit, and reckless abandon as individual development. Strictness was seen as oppression, and order as restraint. Students were accustomed to conspiracy, and indulged in romance. Superficiality and recklessness became almost universal vices. As a result, there was a trend of students choosing teachers at school, and at home, there were loud calls for anti-filial revolution. Even the fundamental norms on which human society relies for maintenance were about to be broken and destroyed. Families could not restrain them, teachers could not control them, and even the power of the government was sometimes exhausted. News of student unrest was reported daily in newspapers. Minor issues could trigger major disturbances. The beginnings of incidents became increasingly strange, causing those running schools to be physically and mentally exhausted, only able to deal with student unrest. The drawbacks of freedom have led to this. Is this what the initiators expected? Seeds of good grain have all become weeds, and roots of fragrant grass have turned into thorns. The nation has been running schools for over thirty years, and the price it has received in return is like this. Concern for the nation is no less than concern for foreign enemies and domestic troubles.

I have carefully considered the crux of the problem and firmly believe that if we want to talk about education today, we must govern Shu like Marquis Wu, using strict measures to awaken self-awareness, and guiding them with principles to return to the normal path. Therefore, I strongly oppose the idea of freedom and adhere to the principle of strictness. Whenever student unrest occurs, I take decisive action. Those who do not follow teachings are given severe sanctions. If the offense is too serious, even if it is near graduation, they will be painfully expelled, never allowing a harmful element to remain just because of their temporary merits. Knowing that bad habits are deeply ingrained, and that the measures implemented may not be effective in transforming people, even if I receive high criticism for this, I will never dare to be lenient to please the public. I have also served as the head of a university, and have always treated young people as friends. I have no intention of harming them. However, because I am responsible for education and know where the problem lies, if I repeat past leniency to gain a reputation for tolerance, and sit idly by while education goes bankrupt without trying to remedy it, how can I live up to the nation's intention in establishing my position, and how can I comfort the heavy responsibility placed upon me by parents and elders? Therefore, I do not seek understanding in advance.

However, education values disciplinary measures, and even more so, positive guidance. It is unreasonable and difficult to feel at ease if there is only punishment without teaching. Therefore, I have promulgated a system that combines teaching and discipline, strictly ordering all schools to conscientiously comply. Regular assessments are also based on this, ensuring that knowledge and action are equally valued. Teachers share the responsibility of moral education, and personal influence and education should have a subtle effect. Teaching people is like supporting a drunk; without much support, they will easily fall. Therefore, the efforts of the school alone are not enough to complete the task of moral education, and I must ask for the full assistance of all parents. Moreover, the decline in academic conduct today has become a deeply rooted problem. Unless administrative agencies, school authorities, and parents work together to remedy it, it will be impossible to achieve the effect of rectification. Today, the number of students in a school is often over a thousand, and at least several hundred. Even with good teachers, there are only a hundred or so. Their eyes and ears may not be able to reach everywhere, and their influence may not be fully effective. School is a group life. If one part is bad, the whole is destroyed. If one person is not good, the whole is tarnished. Therefore, individual training is the basis of group training. Regarding the strengths and weaknesses of students' personalities, changes in their thinking, the quality of their habits, and their diligence in studies, if there are aspects the school cannot fully understand, parents should communicate these, providing guidance. Furthermore, regarding the school's discipline and whether students follow the corrections of teachers, and whether students can improve, the family should also assist and urge them to put the corrections into practice. Only with such wholehearted support can we achieve twice the result with half the effort. Moreover, with morals declining and society becoming polluted, external temptations are abundant, and young people lack the ability to resist. Those who set traps to ensnare them are also everywhere. Sliding into evil is like a landslide; this is human nature. The school's year-round education is no match for society's one-day temptation. Therefore, in life outside of school, it is particularly important for families and schools to jointly guard against and supervise each other to avoid the dangers of straying down the wrong path. I have observed that the higher the grade level, the worse the academic conduct, and the older the age, the less effective the moral education. The virtues cultivated in elementary school are gradually destroyed in middle school, and almost completely disappear in college. The effect of education is reversed, which is deeply regrettable. It is like growing a tree. Elementary school is the beginning of germination, and middle school is the period of forming the trunk. Whether it becomes useful material is determined at this time. Once they enter college, the patterns have been formed, and it is difficult to refine them. Therefore, the strictness of moral education is most important in secondary education, and parental supervision is also essential for middle school students. If supervision is effective and guidance is timely, then everyone can become an excellent child, and everyone can become a useful person. Since the school is an educational institution, the responsibility for moral education is undeniable. The school system, regulations, curriculum, and progress are also uniformly regulated by the government. However, situations may be unfamiliar, attention may be insufficient, execution may be weak, and management may be inadequate. All of these rely on you, parents, to provide guidance, supervision, and assistance, ensuring that families and schools become one, understanding that the success or failure of their children is a matter of personal interest, and viewing the guidance of their children as a shared responsibility. Then, the rectification of academic conduct and the revival of education can be expected soon. Perhaps a small number of parents, witnessing the decline of academic conduct, do not actively assist, but instead passively resist. The result will be that students lose faith in the school, and the school has no way of knowing how to improve. If feelings are alienated, how can the long-term expectations of parents be met? I believe that close contact between families and schools is essential for rectifying academic conduct. Therefore, I have specifically ordered all schools to make every effort to maintain close contact with all parents, and the department has issued a type of form. One is filled out by the school, reporting on the student's academic and behavioral status during the semester to the parents after the end of each semester, and including matters for which the school hopes for parental support. The other is filled out by the parents, reporting to the school on the student's condition at home during the holidays before the start of each semester, and including matters for which the parents hope for support from the school. I deeply understand that the cost of children attending school today is a hundred times what it was in the past. The income of a middle-class family is not enough to cover the cost of one person's education. Most parents endure hardship, live frugally, and work hard to enable their children to study. Therefore, their expectations are certainly different from others. I feel a great sense of responsibility, and therefore, I hope for even more parental assistance. I sincerely hope that you, parents, will wholeheartedly assist in areas where the school authorities fall short. Then, academic conduct will certainly be rectified, learning will be corrected, and students will become pillars of the nation and virtuous children of the family, and both the nation and the family will benefit. I have specifically listed the methods of contact below, hoping that you will consider them favorably.

1. Communicate with the school regularly to express your opinions.

2. Carefully review the school's report form and conscientiously fulfill what the school hopes from parents.

3. Report to the school in detail on the student's extracurricular life and offer concrete suggestions.

4. Schools and parents should jointly organize regular meetings to discuss all educational matters.

5. Be sure to attend the school's parent-teacher conferences.

6. Schools and parents should assist each other as much as possible within the scope of what is feasible. (For example, schools can assist families with writing letters and resolving difficulties, and parents can assist schools by urging their children to abide by school rules and supporting all school facilities.)

The above methods may inevitably be incomplete, but with a spirit of cooperation, there will be no lack of opportunities for cooperation. The key to movement lies in the mind. I hope that you, the parents of all Jiangsu students, will not simply stand aside as spectators, assuming that your children are already under the school's care and management.

Minutes of the Shanghai County Education Bureau Meeting 163

The Shanghai County Education Bureau held its 273rd Bureau Affairs Meeting yesterday afternoon. Those present were Director Shi, Inspector Zhu, Lin Weiwen, Niu Zhiyi, Yang Huiming, Zheng Guozhai, Qian Zhonghou, Zheng Shaoyuan, Xi Siwu, and Wu Jianqing. Director Shi was the chairman, and Pan Xingsan was the recorder. After the formalities, the reported matters were brief. Matters for discussion: (1) The case of Liu Jianhong, Principal of Qiangshu Elementary School, requesting resignation again, was approved. (2) Sun Jixing was appointed as the principal of Qiangshu Elementary School, and Zhou Wenyu was appointed as the principal of Zhuanqiao Elementary School. (3) Omitted. (4) The Zhuanqiao Agricultural Education Center submitted a report on organizing a savings association, which was approved for record. (5) The Department's order to concentrate school properties was to be followed as directed. It was decided to assign Lin Weiwen, Niu Zhiyi, Zheng Guozhai, and Xi Siwu to draft a plan for further discussion. (6) The Zhuanqiao Education Center submitted a report on improving the central tea garden plan and requested approval and allocation of temporary funds. It was decided to handle it after it was included in the budget for the second half of the year. (7) The heads of Lequn Township and Liudao Township in the Second District requested to add a class to Ganlu Elementary School. It was decided to investigate the average attendance of students at the school during this semester, which was less than 30, not meeting the required number of students. Therefore, the request should not be considered. (8) The head of the Wanmin Education Center, Zhu Zuliang, reported that he was beaten by a member of the center, Chou Yunxiang, and requested investigation and requested a record. It was decided to order the head of the center to immediately dismiss the member and, in addition to notifying all relevant departments that the member should never be employed, report to the county for record. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Organization by the Municipal Education Bureau

Health Education Committee 164

The Municipal Education Bureau's central plan for this year, regarding the implementation of health education and implementation methods, has been reported to the municipal government for record. Now, to promote the matter more quickly, a Health Education Committee has been organized, and a draft of the rules of the committee has been prepared and reported to the municipal government for approval and record. The original text of the rules is recorded below: Rules of the Health Education Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau. Article 1: The bureau, for the convenience of implementing health education, has specifically organized a Health Education Committee. Article 2: The number of members of this committee is set at thirteen to nineteen. In addition to the Director of the Municipal Health Bureau and the Director of this Bureau being ex officio members, the rest are appointed or designated by the Director of this Bureau. Article 3: This committee has three standing committee members, who are designated by the Director of this Bureau from among the committee members. Article 4: This committee first establishes two groups, physical education and health, to be responsible for physical education and health matters. Article 5: The physical education and health groups each have two or three standing members, who are designated by the Director of this Bureau. Article 6: Matters involving both physical education and health should be handled jointly by the two groups. Article 7: When the committee is busy, it may establish a number of clerks, who are designated by the Director of this Bureau. Article 8: Meetings of the committee are convened by the standing committee members. Article 9: Detailed rules for the committee and detailed rules for each office are to be determined separately. Article 10: These rules shall be implemented from the date of approval and record by the municipal government.

Shanghai Art College Establishes a Department of Industrial Arts and Design 165

Cultivating Practical Art and Hygiene Talents

Approved by the Ministry of Education

Shanghai Art and Hygiene College has been making vigorous progress in cultivating specialized art and hygiene personnel and art and hygiene education personnel over the years. Recently, it has been promoting industrial arts and hygiene to comply with the central government's aim of adding practical art courses to promote industrial and commercial development. Starting from this semester, in addition to adding practical art courses to the existing five departments, it has also established a Department of Industrial Arts and Design, divided into two groups: [Industrial Arts] and [Advertising Design]. The curriculum focuses entirely on practical art. The school has submitted the curriculum to the Ministry of Education for record and it has been approved by the Ministry of Education under instruction No. 10754. The school is now actively proceeding with the establishment and has begun to enroll new students for both the industrial arts and advertising design groups, with 40 students in each group, all of whom will graduate in three years. The entrance qualification is graduation from senior high school for the science department and those with equivalent qualifications can enter the art department. The curriculum includes, in addition to general courses, practical patterns, practical building decoration, practical carpentry, practical wood practice, loose work method, sheet metal work, gold building, commercial common sense, advertising, practical business decoration methods, etc., so that students can apply their practical skills to society after graduation. Ms. Xique, a female pattern designer from Tokyo, Japan, has been hired as a professor. It is said that the number of applicants in recent days has been quite enthusiastic.

National Games 174

丨Nineteen Provisional Committee Members Appointed丨

Holding a National Shuttlecock Kicking Competition

The Standing Committee of the Physical Education Committee of the Ministry of Education held a meeting in the conference room of the Ministry of Education from 5:00 PM to 7:00 PM on the 18th. Standing committee members Zhang Zhijiang, Chu Minyi, Huang Liming, Zhang Xinfu, and the heads and staff of the ministry were present. Chairman Chu Minyi first reported on the matters at hand and then discussed them. The main decisions were as follows: ㈠ Regarding the proposal to prepare for the National Games in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), nineteen preparatory committee members were appointed to handle the preparations. ㈡ Regarding the proposal to establish a short-term physical education training class, seven committee members were nominated to make preliminary plans. ㈢ Regarding the proposal to hold shuttlecock kicking competitions in the capital and various regions of the country, Chu Minyi was asked to draft the competition rules and submit them to the next Standing Committee meeting for discussion. ㈣ Regarding the proposal to establish detailed curricula and standards for the cultivation of sports talent, committee members Zhang Xinfu, Zhang Zhijiang, Huang Liming, and Chu Minyi were asked to draft them first and then discuss them. ㈤ Regarding the proposal to draft guidelines and award methods for sports as a national policy, Zhang Xinfu was asked to draft the principles, and the Department of Social Affairs was asked to draft the specific regulations. ㈥ Regarding the proposal to draft standards for gradually increasing sports facilities in schools at all levels, a questionnaire would first be conducted, and standards would be set based on the results of the survey. ㈦ Regarding the proposal to conduct trial implementation of sports performance evaluations in various provinces and cities, all committee members were requested to draft methods and send them to the meeting for compilation. ㈧ It was agreed that the next meeting would be held on February 8th.

Spring and Autumn

Violet Chatter 188

— Shou Juan

On the 18th, it snowed all day. This filthy city of Shanghai was cleansed on the surface. Around dusk, I braved the cold and snow to solve the problem of eating. From the hands of a news vendor running around and shouting in the snow, I bought a large newspaper and took it to the YMCA cafeteria to eat and read. Who knew that when I opened the newspaper, there would be a headline with six large characters that caught my eye, reading [All Frozen to Death on the Mountain Peak]. Next to it were three smaller lines: [Volunteer Army of Four Hundred Unyielding to the Death]; [Resisting to the End in Bitter Cold]; [Still Firmly Holding Knives and Guns After Death]. Just these few headlines made me feel a surge of heat rising straight from my core. I murmured the words that Zhang Xun, who defended Tang Dynasty's Yongyang, said to Nan Jiyun: [Nan Ba, a man dies, but he must not yield to injustice!] I thought that our country has four hundred good men who hold knives and guns, freezing to death on the mountain ridge without yielding to injustice. And then, I thought of the other volunteer armies who swallowed ice, bathed in blood, and vowed to kill the enemy. How could this be a sign of national demise? I read this tragic news again and again. Joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness filled my heart, and I could never forget it. And the food I ate stopped in my stomach and could not be digested. I thought this news had the value of being passed down forever to commemorate it. So, with a sincere heart, I respectfully transcribed it as follows:

[The volunteer army of Deng Tiemei, who were trapped in Xiuyan, retreated into Dagushan in mid-December of last year. They built a very solid defensive position on the mountain to resist for a long time. The Japanese army's Kamimura Brigade has been besieging the mountain for more than half a month. On the 11th, the Japanese army sent troops into the mountain to search and found 380 bodies of volunteer soldiers. They refused to surrender to the end. In the bitter cold of minus 20 degrees, they still had to resist strongly. In the end, due to lack of food and thin clothing, they all froze to death. The situation was extremely tragic! Most of the bodies were wearing summer clothes and had been frozen to death for many days. They were still holding knives and guns in their hands. The Japanese army was quite moved.]

Dear readers, what do you think after reading this news? We are all Chinese people. Why do we put the heavy responsibility of [holding weapons to defend the country] entirely on the shoulders of the volunteer army? Where are our millions of brave generals and soldiers who are brave in internal wars? How can those adults and gentlemen who indulge in extravagance, sensuality, and endless dancing and singing face the four hundred soldiers who resisted to the end and froze to death on the mountain ridge? Alas! The four hundred people of Deng's army in Xiuyan are more worthy of weeping and singing than the five hundred people of Tian Heng's island in that year. I would like to buy silk to embroider their deeds, cast gold to record them, and I hope that the country's writers will praise them with poems and articles, and the country's artists will depict them with paintings and sculptures, so that the four hundred people's national spirit will be immortal. Even if China perishes, the spirit of these four hundred people will not be extinguished!

Urban Sketches 189

— Guo Lanxin

Dusk, the time when day and night alternate, the myriad silver lights on the road begin to illuminate the nightlife of the city, where people both enjoy and suffer.

The cold wind roars, flattering the rich and abusing the poor. Cars break through the cold wind and rush to theaters, dance halls, restaurants, hotels, and general meeting places. They go to see plays, enjoy themselves in the green wine and red lights with dancing girls whose bodies tremble, get drunk and full, gather together, make secret appointments, and gamble. In short, it is materialistic enjoyment.

At the same time, the poor in the cold wind are crying with their families in dilapidated alleys and broken houses, suffering from hunger and cold. There are also those who work in the cold wind, hoping for a full meal tomorrow. Under the streetlights, you can also see women who sell their youth and flesh, crushing their souls under the tyrannical power of pimps, hoping that a customer will be their savior in the pit of fire for one day.

Ah, tall buildings and mansions, heavy fur coats, stoves and water heaters, wine and food, cigarettes, women and pleasure. In such an environment, what is there to fear from the cruel cold wind?

Surrounded by hunger and cold, the weeping of wives and children, and the struggle of the poor, there is only one body, boiling with heat, and blood leaping with a red heart to resist the great difficulties given by this era and society.

Urban nightlife continues like this. Will it continue like this forever?

Talking About "Specialization" 190

— Shi Ziqin

I remember when I was a student, there was a very strict Chinese teacher. His nickname was Mr. Despot because he often liked to set essay topics about the word "specialization," such as "A Discussion on Specialization," "A辨 of Arbitrariness," "A 論 of Republic and Despotism"! Not only that, but all the essay topics he set were not allowed to use colloquial language, and had to be written in classical Chinese. So, they gave him this nickname that was [true to his name]. When I did his essays, I always hated not having read the Four Books and Five Classics in my youth, but I had to put together hundreds of words to hand in my paper. At first, I could still deal with his "specialization" topics, but when he set several "specialization" topics in a row, I turned the annotations under the entry of [寸] in the Kangxi dictionary into a new version. I wrote about [Specialization, that is, focusing on one thing, also one thing; professionalism, that is, focusing one's studies on one thing], and came up with a set of [unpleasant texts].

Now, times have changed, and the position of the word "specialization" has been fundamentally shaken. Therefore, [despotism] has died, and all the nouns that are unique to the word [specialization] have been taken away by Western words. For example, [arbitrariness] has been transformed into Fascisti, [professionalism] can be changed to Trust.

What is even more advanced is that the term [focusing one's studies on one thing] is no longer fashionable now. At the very least, it should be renamed [academic omnipotence] or [becoming an official is the first priority, academic is the second].

Not only has the literal meaning of the word [specialization] been occupied, but its meaning has also changed. Look, a universal doctor who can treat [internal medicine, surgery, gynecology, and pediatrics] must put [specializes in all departments] on their sign or business card. If they do not put the word [specialization], people will suspect that their medical skills are not profound.

In short, the word [specialization] is outdated, and there is no need to talk about [focusing on one thing] anymore. However, the [despotism] that has already died is rebelling again. You have to keep an eye on it. The Japanese are shaping and preparing to say goodbye to your lover. Driving the strong enemy out of Shanhaiguan and recovering the lost land in the Northeast is the responsibility of our youth.

The Lover's Honeyed Words and Hidden Dagger 191

— Yan Duoguang

A seductive girl, young men see her, she is as lovely as a beautiful little bird, and as docile as a tame sheep.

A passionate and promising young man, he is drunk in the little bird's nest, in the sheep's den all day long, dissipating the courage to move forward, and falling into the abyss of decadence!

The sound of cannons at Yuguan is heard as the sound of New Year's firecrackers, and the mad shouts of fighting are heard as cheers of celebration. I long for him to wake up soon! I am anxious that he cannot free himself immediately!

I shouted loudly, advising you not to mistake the girl's lipstick for honeyed words, and when you kiss her, you must be aware that after tasting her sweet honeyed words, a sharp sword will be left in your abdomen!

She sucks your blood and absorbs your essence. Her muscles become fuller because she sucks your blood, and her face becomes more delicate because she absorbs your essence. At that time, your blood is dry, and your essence is exhausted. Be careful of the sword in her abdomen! She will turn her head and abandon you in the outer space, causing you to be annoyed, cry bitterly, and go to the dead end of suicide.

Useful young men! Be excited! Do not be drunk in the river of love! You must know that the river of love has thousands of feet of waves, no matter how brave and ambitious you are, it can knock you to the bottom of the sea.

Fiction

Guilty Conscience 192

— Liao Hongshou Juan

The road from the Oriental Villa to the pond was very quiet, but Mr. and Mrs. Dongfang and Ouyang Sheng often came here. In the past, they would sometimes run and laugh, walking back and forth, but now it was different. Xiaoman would call out; [Little otter, is it not good? Let us walk together arm in arm.] So, she took her husband's left hand and the little otter's right hand, and walked and laughed without any scruples. Little otter was often on Xiaoman's lips, ever since the first time she said it jokingly.

I remember one morning, Dongfang Sheng was reading poetry in the study. He had no intention of going out, so only Xiaoman accompanied Ouyang, holding the fishing rod, and went to the pond again. They sat down under a weeping willow. The dew on the shore had not yet dried, and it was all green. He put down the fishing rod and chatted and laughed with Xiaoman. Although the float moved several times, he never picked it up. He praised Xiaoman, saying that her eyes were as lively as fish, and her eyebrows were as slender as the willow leaves on her head. Finally, he murmured for a long time and said, [Man, if I had someone like you to be my companion, I would be willing to sacrifice everything.] Mrs. Dongfang did not take offense at his words. She laughed loudly, threw her head on his shoulder, and stared at Ouyang Sheng's face, laughing at each other. She was laughing at his infatuation, and Ouyang was laughing at her innocence.

At this time, Dongfang Sheng did not know that Ouyang had expressed his love for Xiaoman. This could be seen in several ways. At the same time, although he was very clear about the honesty and purity of the two, he was misunderstood by a note that was accidentally found on Ouyang's desk. There were a few sentences inside: [I am lonely because of you, drifting like a wanderer is not as good, so I am willing to give you a kind of comfort, so that you feel sweet even in your dreams. You sometimes talk very sickeningly, I do not ask. But please avoid the front of the parrot, because I do not hope that the parrot learns to be as frivolous as you.] He recognized Xiaoman's handwriting and could not help but feel sad.

A sick person cannot withstand stimulation the most. In this situation, Dongfang Sheng gradually became thinner. His old illness was mixed with new sorrows, and he only felt heavier and heavier. Ouyang Sheng ran to the city every day to seek doctors and buy medicine, but Dongfang Sheng showed no improvement. Time was approaching late autumn again. One day, Dongfang Sheng asked Xiaoman and Ouyang to accompany him to the pond. On the road, they were still walking side by side, but they were not laughing and talking. Dongfang Sheng inspected the pond for a week. The willow leaves were floating all over the pond, covering the ripples. He smiled bitterly and said to the sky; [My Lord, let me return myself to you here.] (II)

A Record of Scenic Exploration in Yi-nan (Part Two) 193

— Zhu Shouren

丨A Tour of the Shanjuan Cave丨

After a moment of sightseeing, Mr. Chu led the tour to the upper cave (also known as the Warm Cave, or the Great Qi Sea). The cave entrance is level with the wall and connected to the rear of the middle cave. At the entrance, there are stone steps on both sides to ascend. The moonlight is hazy, and the clouds and mist fly about! It is a separate world, seemingly not of this earth. It is approximately ten acres in size, divided into upper and lower levels, like a stage with side buildings. Two large, natural stone pillars stand majestically within it. Five or six gas lamps are lit inside the cave. Viewing them from several dozen feet away, it is like glimpsing distant stars through the gaps in the clouds. Stone steps wind around, twisting and turning. The mountain air is abundant, the walls are moist and glistening, and it is warm like entering a bathhouse. Coupled with the fragrance of Phoebe zhennan freshly steamed, the fragrant mist is rich. I then realized that the moonlight and flying clouds I saw earlier were merely illusions created by the mountain air and lamplight. Mr. Chu said, "This air is only present in winter, and it is even more intense when it is severely cold. Even if one is naked, one does not feel the cold during heavy snowfall. If one tours at night with torches, the illusions are numerous, creating a wonderful scene of clouds and mist, truly marvelous!" Relying on electric torches, we followed the stone steps, circling back and forth, ascending and descending several times, yet still could not discern its capacity.

After the tour, we turned back to the Luoyan Small Abode and then proceeded to the lower cave. The cave is higher than the middle cave. At its highest point, a thousand-foot electric torch is needed to illuminate it. In front is a small waterfall called Yin Jian. Although the water is not vast, the moss is green and dripping, and the melody of the spring bursts forth. Inside the cave, strange rocks jut out, steep cliffs and hard rocks display unusual formations, piled up and hanging upside down from the cave ceiling. If even a slight gust of wind were to move them, they might fly away with the white clouds. On the walls, unusual rocks are formed into the shape of pine trees, with straight trunks reaching the sky and horizontal branches supporting a canopy. Going further inside, it gradually narrows, becoming dark and secluded, with nothing visible. It extends for three miles to reach the rear cave, but unfortunately, we did not venture to explore it. Returning to the Luoyan Small Abode, Mr. Chu had already prepared tea and refreshments, awaiting us. During the meal, he delivered a welcoming speech, which was responded to by Mr. Yao Yuangan, a member of the Standing Committee of the delegation.

After a brief rest, we exited the Chaoxu Hall, crossed a small ridge, and reached the rear cave (also known as the Water Cave). The cave is located at the foot of the mountain, several yards wide, only a few feet high, shaped like a crescent moon, with wisteria and vines like curtains, flying smoke hanging dimly. A clear stream flows straight into the cave. A small boat is moored at the entrance, capable of holding eight people. The boatman held a torch in his hand while rowing. Those who arrived first among the members eagerly boarded the boat. Wielding the oars, we entered, and after about twenty minutes, emerged. Inside the cave, the passage twists and turns, reaching a depth of sixty yards. In high places, it can be about ten feet tall, while in low places, one must crouch in the boat to pass through. The stone patterns are mottled, and it is gloomy and cold, like entering the underworld. Regrettably, due to the large number of people and limited time, it was difficult to explore thoroughly. In total, we entered twice, carrying eighteen people. By then, it was past three o'clock. I arrived late and was unable to join in. However, reserving this as a voucher for a future visit is also a great thing. I then bid farewell to Mr. Chu, made arrangements for a visit to Gengsang the next day, boarded the boat, and arrived in Yi at eight o'clock at night.

丨A Tour of the Gengsang Cave丨

On the sixth morning, we went to the East Gate to board a boat. The route went through the East Jiu River, where the waterway was relatively narrow and there were many boats traveling back and forth. We first arrived at the Shushan to view the Zisha (purple clay) kilns, and at noon, we docked at Huwenzhen. We disembarked and walked about seven miles, arriving at the Chaoyang Taoist Temple, where an image of Zhang Gong (Lord Zhang) is enshrined. There is a Gan Quan (Sweet Spring) stele in the temple. Further on, we arrived at the Gengsang Cave on Mengfeng Mountain. The cave was where Zhou Kangcangzi (Master Kangcang of Zhou) lived in seclusion, Gengsang being his courtesy name. The Records of Local Customs by Zhou Chu state that Zhang Daoling of the Han Dynasty cultivated the Tao here, hence it is also known as Zhang Gong Cave. Some say it was where Guo Lao (Immortal Guo) attained enlightenment, but details are impossible to ascertain. Mr. Chu and others were already waiting for us there. They led us to the rear cave, which was very high and spacious, with dozens of stone steps leading directly to a platform. Then, crossing the Dafan (Great Fan) ridge, we turned to the front cave, named Tianbian Dachang (Heavenly Bamboo Field), which was as large as ten acres, as open as a large building. Stalactites hung down, pure and bright, the large ones several embraces around, the small ones filling a grasp, like dangling baby necklaces, like hanging crown tassels, like dragon whiskers, like tiger teeth, like fluttering pearl banners, like icicles dripping from the eaves, exquisite and strange, indescribable. The name "Heavenly Necklace" is no exaggeration. At the cave's upper entrance, various trees were lush and green, and a subtle fragrance assailed the nostrils. Sunlight shone through, making one feel like an immortal. Stone steps of varying heights on both sides spiraled in all directions, like walking on a perilous plank road, like climbing a ladder to heaven. The scenery circled around, leading directly to the mountain ridge. Looking back at the cave entrance, it was like a giant monster opening its mouth, as if wanting to choose someone to devour, to grease its sharp teeth. After the climb, Mr. Chu had already laid out fruits, snacks, fragrant tea, and refreshments in the Tianbian Dachang, welcoming us. We then all partook of the tea and snacks. Mr. Chu briefly described the scenic spots in the cave and the transportation situation. Tax Commissioner Yang Mingxin and renowned painter Hu Boxiang also gave speeches one after another.

American Cotton Declines, British and Indian Cotton Tend Higher 217

Yesterday, American cotton lacked buyers, and Liverpool news was unfavorable. Wall Street was buying, and the market was sluggish. Futures fell by 9 to 13 points, and spot prices fell by 10 points. British cotton futures rose 3 points, and spot prices rose 7 points. Egyptian cotton spot prices rose 12 points. Indian cotton initially rose with American cotton, but later weakened due to profit-taking by bulls and selling by speculators. Pingguo’er rose 1.5 rupees, and Aomula and Bailuoxi rose 2 rupees. Original telegrams are as follows (dated the 18th):

Grains

Approaching the Lunar New Year, the Rice Market in Shanghai... 218

Sales are sluggish except for glutinous rice, which saw a price increase of half a yuan.

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the weather turned warmer, and the ice in the inland rivers began to thaw, so rice boats arrived in Shanghai in succession, totaling more than 70. However, retail sales were still weak, and the market situation turned soft, with prices falling slightly. There was a shortage of rice in Tongli, with prices opening at around 9 yuan and 45 cents. Sutong and Changbang Nangang Qingjiao rice prices decreased slightly. The season for Du Yangjian rice is approaching, and it is feared that there will be a shortage in the interior. Yin Yuan rice was selling somewhat, so the market price was able to stand firm. Only Bian Yuan rice stood out, with a price increase of half a yuan, due to the temporary shortage.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, more than 20 boats of spot goods arrived from the river, but sales were very sluggish. As the Lunar New Year is approaching, the stores are facing tight credit conditions, which has led to sluggish activity. The market for North Bang white japonica rice was slightly weak, and medium-grade white japonica rice fell by 20 cents. There were not many arrivals of Yangxian rice, and retail sales were slightly active, with prices increasing by 10 to 20 cents. There were no arrivals of Bai Yuan rice, and the price remained firm. Du Xian and Yin Yuan were stable. There were no arrivals of Bu Xian rice. There were slight arrivals of late rice, and the price also fell by 10 to 20 cents. Kexian rice remained firm.

(Outgoing) The Shanghai Rice Industry Association has received a total of 330,000 bags of passports for both the North and South Seas, with about 70,000 bags for the South Seas and the rest for the North Seas.

Flour Market Plunges in the Afternoon 219

Yesterday, the flour market showed a generally stable trend in the morning for all months. Although the quoted price of foreign wheat fell slightly by about 20 cents, the current flour supply was tight. Although there was no risk of a short squeeze for the current month, the bulls were unwilling to let go, so the prices for January and February were both tight, improving by about 1 cent compared to the previous day's closing price. Long-term prices remained stable. However, when the market opened in the afternoon, the market for all months suddenly took a sharp turn downwards. It was heard that the pricing of Australian wheat by foreign firms suddenly loosened, with February shipments as low as 3 taels and 6 mace, and delivery in Nanjing was only 3 taels, 6 mace and 1 fen. However, as the year-end was approaching, large and small factories were unwilling to trade. At that time, Fuxin also slightly sold off, so near-term and long-term prices both plunged step by step. Given the continued oversupply of foreign wheat, changes should be guarded against in the future. As a result, the current month fell by 1.5 fen compared to the previous day, February fell by 2.75 fen, March fell by 2.5 fen, April fell by 1.25 fen, May fell by 1.75 fen, and June fell by a small amount.

Australian Wheat Prices Loosen

Wheat Futures Market Leans Towards Selling 220

Yesterday was the last day before the market closed for the major year-end break. Activity was brisk, but market prices were low due to low foreign wheat spot and futures prices, and people were expecting declines. The price of Australian wheat for February shipments at 3 taels and 6 mace further influenced the market. Sellers were even more active. Other bulls directly settled and took delivery of 500 tons of foreign wheat, which was acquired by Huafeng. The closing price for wheat futures was slightly down by 2 fen for January, slightly down by 1 fen for February, slightly down by 5 fen for March, and slightly down by 3 fen for April. There were no transactions for the remaining months.

Kexian Rice Sees Sluggish Activity in Both Sales and Purchases at Year-End 221

| Chen Xiao Rice Was Sold by Anli for 2,000 Bags |

(Kexian) Yesterday, both arrivals and sales of Kexian rice were sluggish. Although a few arrivals reached Shanghai, the owners intended to hoard and not sell, waiting for a favorable price in the red market after the New Year. However, sales were sluggish in all areas, as the end of the major closing period was approaching, and all parties in the local Kexian market intended to close their books. Only the Fuzhou and Quanzhou areas were still interested in trading, but they were not eager to buy, and were determined not to buy unless the price was low. Yesterday, 700 bags of Hunan machine-milled rice were cleverly sold in the market for 9 yuan, 1 jiao and 7 fen, or 3 li and 1 jiao. This price was slightly lower than the previous market price. The market price should have been above 9 yuan and 2 jiao. Due to the urgent need for year-end funds, the price was relatively cheap.

(Foreign Rice) There have been no transactions for a long time, because buyers and sellers have not been able to reach a price. Yesterday, Anli Foreign Firm suddenly sold 2,000 bags of old Xiao rice, which was acquired by the trader Guojin at a price of 8 yuan, which seemed to have risen slightly compared to the previous price. There was no intention to trade futures, for fear of repeating the losses of the previous year.

Chicago Wheat Weakens Again 222

Chicago telegram on the 18th: Wheat first rose due to buying from the East, then fell due to weakness on Wall Street. A total of 20 million bushels were traded on the 17th. The market prices on the 18th are listed below:

Metals 223

The market is sluggish and shows a closing-down scene. Yesterday, the metal market was characterized by a lack of transactions from various dealers, showing a trend of closing down. Except for factories adding some new patterns, most of the transactions await the beginning of the Lunar New Year. As for the arrival of goods, dealers had already reduced their orders due to the year-end credit crunch, therefore, the supply of tinplate, white lead sheet, and new lead wire may be inadequate. It is predicted that prices will rise steadily in the coming days. Other items, such as new silver dollars, silver dollar heads, and silver ingots, are mostly declining due to oversupply. The prices of other foreign products do not show significant fluctuations.

Silk and Tea: Tea Market Continues to Be Quiet 224

Yesterday, the tea market in Shanghai continued to be quiet. Most foreign dealers have been taking a wait-and-see attitude because the large batch of Fine Eyebrow tea cables sent out last week has not been responded to. Only the Tongfu Foreign Firm and China Tea Company bought 200 boxes of Wuzhuang Fine Eyebrow tea, with Wudong Fine Eyebrow tea priced at 58 taels, and Wubei Fine Eyebrow tea priced at 70 to 110 taels, with no price changes compared to the previous days. In addition, the large dealers also made scattered replenishments of Mei Xi tea produced by the Chinese tea factory. Otherwise, there were no transactions.

Coal and Coal Dust Sales Are Particularly Sluggish 225

Yesterday, the transaction volume of various types of bituminous coal and white coal in the coal market was quite large. However, the sales of various types of coal dust were particularly sluggish. Because factories were shutting down for the end of the lunar year, the purchase of bituminous coal dust was rare. The purchase of white coal dust was hampered by icy weather, and many suffered losses. Therefore, the industry was reluctant to purchase. The prices have loosened slightly. Fushun dust was 5 taels, Yuanshan dust was 5 taels, Gaowei dust was 5 taels and 5 mace, Jingxing dust was 10 taels, Huadong dust was 6 taels, Mac dust was 7 taels and 8.5 mace, and Haifeng dust was 7 taels and 7.5 mace.

Miscellaneous: Overseas Telegraphic News Roundup 226

(Sugar Market) New York, 18th, telegraph: The spot market is loose, and prices are generally showing a slight decline. The price is 6.875 cents per pound. Futures for January remain unchanged, while March, May, and September are down 2 points, and July and December are down 1 point. According to a London cable, March sugar futures rose by 1.25 pence, May rose by 0.75 pence, and August rose by 1.25 pence. Javanese white sugar remained unchanged at 7 shillings and 9 pence (per 120 pounds).

(Metals) London cable: Antimony and zinc remain unchanged, tin and zinc rise slightly, and lead declines slightly. New York copper prices remain unchanged at 5.00.

(Grains) London cable: Chinese soybeans rise slightly to 18 shillings and 9 pence per ton. Peanuts (with shells) are 14.3 (per 120 pounds), and gallnuts are 43.00 (per 120 pounds).

(Oil Market) New York cable: Sesame oil is 4.375, peanut oil is 8, soybean oil is 4, and rapeseed oil is 36 (all in US cents).

(Silk Market) New York cable: The silk market is erratic due to a lack of reliable data. Prices are therefore flat. Transactions and Exchange Street are weak and looser. 153 contracts were traded (10 bales per contract). Japanese silk spot prices fell by 23 points. Chinese and Italian silks remained unchanged.
